650	<h2 class="blog_entry-title"> Md. Abu Siddique Vs.  D. M. Habibur Rahman and other, (Md. Moinul Islam Chowdhury, J.)	   </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 1896 of 2016 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Moinul Islam Chowdhury, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Sheikh Muhammed Serajul Islam, Advocate,  Mr. Mahfujur Rahman Roman with Mr. M. Nahiyan Ibn Subhan, Advocates,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ  	 </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Abu Siddique</p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  D. M. Habibur Rahman and others </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2018-06-02</p><!DOCTYPE html><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"> </p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; width: 201px;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 94.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Md. line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">05.02.2018</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 8.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 74.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> Abu Siddique</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">. . . Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">D. M. Habibur Rahman and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">... Opposite parties </span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">gymwjg weevn I ZvjvK (wbeÜb) wewagvjv, 2009</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">wewa 13</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">A person cannot be a Nika Registrar for more than one Union Parishad but the present petitioner has been a Nika Register for two unions which is not permissible under the above new law. The settled principle in this regard is that everyone must be abide by the law introduced for any purpose and the present petitioner cannot get any benefit which the prevailing law does not permit.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">       </span>. . .(12)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Order 7, Rule 11(d)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">gymwjg weevn I ZvjvK (wbeÜb) wewagvjv, 2009</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">wewa 13</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">A suit cannot be allowed to continue if the suit is barred by any law under the provision of Order 7 Rule 11(d) of the Code of Civil Procedure. In the present case therefore the suit is barred by law as the present plaintiff petitioner claimed a relief in the year of 2013 for injunction and for allowing him to function as Nika Registrar </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">of Palerchar in contravention to the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>provision</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> of law. . . . (12)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Sheikh Muhammed Serajul Islam, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . For the Petitioner </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Mahfujur Rahman Roman with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. M. Nahiyan Ibn Subhan, Advocates</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . For the Opposite Party No. 1</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Md. Moinul Islam Chowdhury</span></u></strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">, J:</span></u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> At the instance of the present plaintiff-opposite party-petitioner, Md. Abu Siddique, a leave was granted and this Rule has been issued calling upon the opposite party No. 1 to show cause as to why the judgment and order dated 28.10.2015 passed by the learned Additional District Judge, Shariatpur, in Civil Revision No. 13 of 2014 allowing the aforesaid revision and thereby reversing the judgment and order dated 30.04.2014 passed by learned Assistant Judge, Jajira, Shariatpur in Title Suit No. 128 of 2013 rejecting the application under Order VII, Rule 11(d) of the Code of Civil Procedure, should not be set aside. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The relevant facts for disposal of this Rule, <em>inter-alia</em>, are that the present petitioner as the plaintiff filed the Title Suit No. 128 of 2013 in the Court of learned Assistant Judge, Jajira, Shariatpur for a decree for permanent injunction to restrain the opposite party from appointing a Nika Registrar and also for a declaration to allow him to continue as a Nika Registgrar of Palerchar Union, Police Station-Jajira, Shariatpur. The plaint contains that the present plaintiff petitioner was appointed as a Nika Registrar for the Unions of Bilashpur, Kundarchar and Palerchar by the Ministry of Law and Parliamentary Affairs of the People Republic of Bangladesh on 18.08.1998, which was confirmed by the District Nika Registrar, Shariatpur on 02.09.1998. While he has been performing his duties Kunderchar Union went under river Padma by way of river erosion and the peoples of the said union moved away. The petitioner thereafter filed Writ Petition No. 4545 of 2003 in this court where a direction was given to issue permanent license for two unions namely Bilashpur and Palerchar. On 31.01.2013 a letter was issued by the defendant No. 6, Senior Assistant Secretary, Ministry of Law directing the sub-registrar of Jajira to appoint the defendant No.7, the present opposite party No. 1 as the Nika Registrar for the Union of palerchar as per the provisions of law published by a Gazette notification dated 10.08.2009. The plaintiff filed the suit challenging the said appointment.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The suit has been contested by the present opposite party No. 1, D. M. Habibur Rahman as the defendant No. 7 by filing a written statement and denying the statement made in the plaint and contending that the defendants (the authority) properly appointed Nika Registrar to the present opposite Party No. 1 for the Union of Palercar under the provisions of law. The present opposite party No. 1 also filed an application under Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure for rejecting the plaint as the suit was barred by law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">After hearing the parties the learned trial court rejected the application by his order dated 30.04.2014. Being aggrieved the present opposite party No. 1, as the applicant filed the Civil Revision No. 13 of 2014 in the court of learned District Judge, which was heard by the learned Additional District Judge, Shariatpur on transfer who by his judgment and order dated 28.10.2015 allowed the revision by setting aside the order passed by the learned trial court. This revisional application has been filed under Section 115(4) of the Code of Civil Procedure challenging the legality of the said order and a leave was granted and this Rule was issued thereupon. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Sheikh Muhammed Serijul Islam, the learned Advocate, appearing for the petitioner submits that it is clear from the plaint that the suit is not barred by any law but the court below failed to evaluate the same, thus, committed an error of law resulting in an error in the decision occasioning failure of justice.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The learned Advocate also submits that the present petitioner filed the Writ Petition No. 4545 of 2003 which was partly made absolute directing to appoint the petitioner in two union parishads under Police Station- Jajira but the appointment of the present opposite party No. 1 by the Ministry of Law and Parliamentary Affairs has been violation of the direction given by this court and the suit should be allowed to dispose of on merit instead of by rejecting the plaint, therefore, the learned trial court after considering the pleadings rejected the application but the learned revisional court below committed an error of law by allowing the application filed under Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code of Civil<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Procedure, as such, this court should interfere for the ends of justice and the Rule should be made absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The Rule has been opposed by the present opposite party No. 1.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Mahfujur Rahman Roman, the learned Advocate, appearing along with the learned Advocate Mr. M. Nahiyan Ibn Subhan, appearing for the opposite party No. 1, submits that the learned trial court rejected the application filed by the present opposite party under Order 7<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Rule<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>11 of the Code of Civil Procedure on the basis of the direction of Writ Petition which was passed in the year of 2005 but without considering the subsequent enforcement of law in the year of 2009, therefore, came to a wrongful conclusion. However, the learned<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>revisional court below after considering the prevailing law came to a lawful conclusion to allow the revision by setting aside the judgment and order passed by the learned trial court below, as such, this court should not interfere upon the judgment and order passed by the revisional court below and the Rule should be discharged.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The learned Advocate also submits that the present petitioner was appointed by the concern authority in the year of 1998 for three unions but after the enforcement of Rule 13 (Umo) of “</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-ansi-language: EN;">j¤p¢mj ¢hh¡q J a¡m¡L (¢ehåe) ¢h¢dj¡m¡, 2009</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">” a person cannot be a Nika Registrar in more than one union parishad therefore the judgment and order in the Writ Petition in the year of 2005 became inoperative by the subsequent introduction of new law in the year of 2009 thus the Rule should be discharged.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Considering the above submissions made by the learned Advocates appearing for the respective parties and also considering the revisional application filed under Section 115 (4) of the Code of Civil Procedure, in particular, the impugned judgment and order passed by the revisional court below, it appears to me, that the present petitioner as the plaintiff filed a suit for permanent injunction restraining the Government opposite parties from appointing the present opposite party No.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>1 and also for a declaration permitting the present petitioner to continue functioning as the Nika Registrar for two unions namely Bilashpur and Palerchar under Police Station-Jajira, District-Shariatpur. The present opposite party No. 1, D.M. Habibur Rahman contested the suit by filing a written statement and also by filing an application under Order 7 Rule 11 of the Cod of Civil Procedure contending that the suit was barred by the law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In the above given factual aspects in this case, this court has to take a decision as to whether the suit filed by the present petitioner was actually barred by law or not. In order to take a decision in this matter I have carefully examined the available documents in the revisional application. I found that the suit was filed by the present petitioner claiming injunction and also seeking<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>a relief to continue function as Nika Registrar for two unions namely Bilashpur and Palerchar as per his appointment in the year of 1998. In this regard, this court seemed to have directed to give a permanent appointment to the petitioner in the said two unions, however, the court has also given liberty to the concern authority to appoint as per the provision of law. While the petitioner has been performing his function as Nika Registrar the law changed by introducing “</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-ansi-language: EN;">j¤p¢mj ¢hh¡q J a¡m¡L (¢ehåe) ¢h¢dj¡m¡, 2009</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">” and it was introduced under the authority given under<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Section 14 of the Muslim Marriages and divorces (Registration) Act, 1974 (Act No. LII of 1974). The said Bidhemala contains Rule 13, which reads as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">“</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-ansi-language: EN;">13z A¢d­®rœz- HC ¢h¢dj¡m¡l Ad£e fËcš ¢eL¡qÚ ®l¢SÖY~Ê¡­­®ll m¡C­®p­¾p k¡q¡ ¢LR¤C b¡L¥L e¡ ®Le, HLSe ¢eL¡qÚ ®l¢SøÊÊ¡l­®L ¢ejÀh¢ZÑa Hm¡L¡l SeÉ m¡C­®p¾p fË¡ce Ll¡ k¡C­®h, kb¡x-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(L) ¢p¢V L­®fÑ¡®­ln®­el ®r®­œ, HL¢V<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Ju¡XÑ;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(M) "L' ®nËZ£l ®­f±lpi¡l ®r­®œ, c¤C¢V Ju¡XÑ;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(N) "M' ®nËe£l ®f±lpi¡l ®r­®œ, ¢ae¢V<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Ju¡XÑ;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(O) "N' ®nËZ£l ®f±lpi¡l ®r®­œ pjNË Hm¡L¡;</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(P) CE¢eue f¢loc Hm¡L¡l ®r®­œ HL¢V CE¢euez</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">From the above provisions of law for Nika Registrar, a person cannot be a Nika Registrar for more than one union parishad but the present petitioner has been a Nika Register for two unions which is not permissible under the above new law. The settled principle in this regard is that everyone must be abide by the law introduced for any purpose and the present petitioner cannot get any benefit which the prevailing law does not permit. Accordingly, the petitioner lost his relief given by this court in the Writ Petition by the introduction of subsequent law in the year of 2009. A suit cannot be allowed to continue if the suit is barred by any law under the provision of Order 7 Rule 11(d) of the Code of Civil Procedure. In the present case therefore the suit is barred by law as the present plaintiff petitioner claimed a relief in the year of 2013for injunction and for allowing him to function as Nika Registrar of Palerchar in contravention to the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>provision of law, as such, I consider that the suit should not be allowed<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>to continue any further as it is barred by law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The learned trial court came to a wrongful</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> conclusion only on the directions given by this </span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">court in a Writ Petition in the year of 2005 and <span style="letter-spacing: .4pt;">the learned trial court failed to consider the </span></span><span style="font-size: 11pt;">prevailing law applicable in the suit therefore committed an error of law, however, the learned revisional court considered the relevant facts in this case and the applicable law, therefore, came to a lawful conclusion to allow the revisional application by setting aside the judgment and order of the trial court. I am therefore not inclined to interfere into the judgment and order passed by the learned revisional courts below.</span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">14.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Accordingly, I do not find merit in the Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">15.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In the result, the Rule is discharged. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">16.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In view of the above discussion the present opposite party No. 1, D. M Habibur Rahman, son of D.M. Abu Sayeed shall function as the Nika Registrar of the Palerchar union parishad, under Police Station- Jajira, District-Shariatpur as per the appointment given on 31.01.2013 by the Senior Assistant Secretary, Ministry of Law by the present opposite party No. 6. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">17.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">However it appears to this court that the union parishad of Bilashpur has been seriously effected by river erosion wherein the present petitioner, Md. Abu Siddique, son of late Md. A. Karim lost his enough opportunities of his function as Nika Registrar therefore the present opposite party Nos. 5, 6 and 7 may consider his  area  to function in an adjacent union in the event of any vacancy in future because of the fact of erosion most of the areas of Bilashpur union parishad.   </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">18.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The interim order of stay granted at the time of issuance of the Rule upon the operation of the judgment and order dated 28.10.2015 passed by the learned Additional District Judge, Shariatpur in Civil Revision No. 13 of 2014 is hereby recall and vacated. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">19.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The Section is directed to communicate this judgment and order to the court concern immediately.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">         Ed.  </span></strong></p><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue%20__August__18(2)__C.%20R.%201896%20of%2016_Md.%20Moinul%20Islam%20Chowdhury,%20J.__1.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Revision No. </span></strong></a><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">1896 of 2016</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
651	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Azad Rahman and another Vs. The State, (Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarker , J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 47693 of 2017  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Rezaul Haque, J And Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Devision ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. AF Hassan Ariff, Senior Advocate with Mr. Nabil Ahsan, Advocates ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2017</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Azad Rahman and another  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  The State </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Criminal Procedure </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-01</p><!DOCTYPE html><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; font-variant: small-caps; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(criminal miscellaneous jurisdiction)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; height: 192px; margin-right: auto;" width="664"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 297.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Md. Rezaul Haque, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">And</strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J</strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">13.12.2017</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 56.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue%20__AUGUST_18(2)__Crl.%20Misc.%2047693%20of%2017__Muhammad%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarkar,%20J.__10.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 266.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Azad Rahman and another </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: right;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . Accused Petitioners</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The State </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .Opposite-Party</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 526 (1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">It is not possible for any Court to define the expression ‘for the ends of justice’ in the fixed words and, thus, it would be an improper step for this Court to endeavour to lay down any guideline of the situations which may cover the said expression. Upon meticulously examining particular fact and circumstance of a case, when a Court arrives at a conclusion that there is no specific statutory provision in place which may fit in with the stated fact/circumstance for transferring the case from the concerned trial Court to a competent Court, but the conscience of a Judge, at the same<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>time, dictates to hold a view that the case should be transferred from the present trial Court to a competent Court for ensuring a fair trial, that situation may be called/termed to be a situation when this Court ‘for the ends of justice’ should pass necessary order/s for conducting the trial of the case either by the equivalent/superior Court of the same District or by the equivalent/superior Court of a different District or by the High Court Division itself.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                  </span>. . .(12)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 526 (1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">If the allegations are taken to be true and, as per the prayer of the petitioners, the case is transferred to the District of Dhaka, the petitioners cannot guarantee that the same situation would not be created by the Minister in Dhaka; rather it would be convenient for the Minister to monitor the case and, thereby, influence the same. ...(13)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 526 (1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Courts of Bangladesh are independent in dealing with any case and, if at any point of time, when a Judge is unduly communicated and pressured by the executive or by any person, the concerned trial Court Judge’s duty is either to deal with the matter by her/himself towards punishing the contemnor or to report the same to the Registrar of this Court.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                     </span>. . . (14)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 526 (1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Trial of a case should not be held in the present Court for securing ‘the ends of justice’ or for mitigating the situations set out in clauses (a) to (d) of Section 526(1) of the CrPC, then, this Court may pass necessary order/s to transfer it either to any equivalent criminal Court or to a Court of Sessions or to itself. Litigants must approach this Court/Sessions Judge with clean hands in availing the discretionary relief under Section 526 of the CrPC. In a fit and proper </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">case, this Court shall never hesitate to transfer</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> the trial of a case from the concerned Court </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">to any competent Court for the sake of justice. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">At the same time, this Court owes a constitutional</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> duty of maintaining a discipline in the administration of justice in the subordinate judiciary of this country.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>. . .(17)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Section 526 (6A)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 105%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">The propensity of the litigants to transfer the trial of a case from the concerned trial Court to another Court on omnibus ground requires to be trimmed down for the sake of administration of justice of this land and, </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">which is why, the Legislature has empowered</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;"> this Court to punish an applicant who intends to waste the invaluable time of this </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Court by filing trivial or fallacious application</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;"> for transferring a case from the present Court to another Court.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                           </span>. . .(17)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">Mr. AF Hassan Ariff, Senior Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Nabil Ahsan, Advocates</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the petitioners</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> Md.</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> Khurshedul Alam, D.A.G </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . For the State<u></u></span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J: </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Pursuant to an application filed by the accused-petitioners under Section 526 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898 (CrPC), this Rule was issued calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why the Kot Druto G.R. Case No. 40 of 2015 arising out of Kotchandpur Police Station Case No. 08 dated 29.07.2015, under Sections 4(1)/5 of the Ain Srinkhola Bighnokari Aporadh Damon Ain, 2002 (as amended in 2014), now pending before the Senior Judicial Magistrate, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Jhenaidah (Druto Bichar Adalat at Jhenaidah), should not be transferred to any competent Court within the District of Dhaka.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The prosecution case, in short, is that one Md. Saiful Islam Litu, as a complainant, filed a complaint petition before the Senior Judicial <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Magistrate, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Jhenaidah, under Sections</span> 4(1)/5 of the Ain Srinkhola Bighnokari Aporadh Damon Ain, 2002. It was alleged in <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">the said complaint-petition that the complainant</span> is a farmer who was accorded permission by the Government for purchasing power tillers at a 25% subsidized rate to sell the same to the real cultivators at the said subsidized price. The accused-petitioners are journalists who demanded extortion of Tk. 1,50,000/- from the complainant threatening him to publish a news regarding the selling of the power tillers to the persons other than cultivators and, out of fear and anxiety, the complainant gave Tk. 20,000/- <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">to the accused-petitioners. However, the accused</span>-petitioners threatened the complainant to publish news if the balance amount is not paid. Later on, when the complainant declined to make any further payment, the accused-petitioners on 02.06.2015 published a false news in the Daily Prothom Alo. To this end, an inquiry was carried out by the Ministry of Agriculture and the inquiry committee of the ministry found the news to be false. Thereafter, when the complainant published a rejoinder in the Daily Somokal on 06.07.2015 against the said false news, the accused-petitioners kept threatening the complainant to publish further false news, which compelled the complainant to lodge this case. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Upon going through the above complaint</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-petition, the learned Magistrate directed the Officer-in-Charge of Kotchandpur Police Station to treat it as an FIR and to do the needful. Accordingly, the FIR was registered as Kotchandpur Police Station Case No. 08 dated 29.07.2015 and, thereafter, the same was forwarded to the learned Judicial Magistrate, cognizance Court Jhenaidah, where the case was registered as Kot Druto GR Case No. 40 of 2015. On 19.08.2015, the Police submitted charge sheet no. 72 dated 10.08.2015 and on 25.08.2015, the accused-petitioners voluntarily surrendered before the Magistrate and obtained bail and on 14.10.2015, the case was transferred for trial to the Court of Senior Judicial Magistrate, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Jhenaidah in which the power and jurisdiction of the Druta Bichar Adalat of Jhenaidah has been vested. Thereafter, on 22.11.2015 the trial Court (the Druto Bichar Adalat) framed charge under Section 4 of the Ain Srinkhola Bighnokari Aporadh Damon Ain, 2002 (as amended in 2014) against the accused-petitioners and, by now, 6 (six) witnesses have been examined. It is stated that on 29.05.2017 the case was fixed for examination of witnesses and, on the said day, upon hearing the accused-petitioners’ application for staying all further proceedings of the case when the learned Judge of the Druta Bichar Adalat was passing the stay order, he uttered that “Please </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">Avcbviv GLvb †_‡K gvgjv mwi‡q wbb</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">”. Thereafter on 04.07.2017, when the accused-petitioners prayed for adjournment of the case, the learned Judge again uttered that “</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: SutonnyMJ;">GLvb †_‡K gvgjv e`wj K‡i wbb</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">”. For the above reasons, the accused-petitioners filed this miscellaneous case praying for transferring the aforesaid case from Jhenaidah to Dhaka and obtained the instant Rule. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. AF Hassan Ariff, the learned Senior Advocate, appearing for the accused-petitioners at the very outset draws our attention to the comments passed by the learned Judge of the trial Court (the Druta Bichar Adalat) in course of hearing of the application filed by the accused-petitioners for staying further proceedings and again, on another day, in the midst of hearing of the application for adjournment and submits that the learned Judge is not feeling comfortable to conduct trial of the case. He, then, contends that the news which gave rise to the case is against the Ministry of Agriculture and from the subsequent conduct of the concerned Ministry, the accused-petitioners have cogent reason to believe that at the behest of the Minister of the said Ministry the case was initiated and at her direction, the local political leaders are constantly pursuing the case and on each and every date a number of the local political leaders and workers appear in the Court premises and use intangible filthy language to the accused-petitioners and from such activities of the local political leaders and supporters, there has been a reasonable apprehension in the mind of the accused-petitioners that the Government officials at the Ministry of Agriculture are acting against the accused-petitioners and a fair and impartial trial cannot be held in the aforesaid trial Court. Mr. Ariff lastly submits that inordinate delay in disposing of this case indicates that this false case is filed for harassing the accused-petitioners inasmuch as this case is a case of Druto Bichar Ain and the trial of the case was supposed to have been completed within the shortest possible time prescribed in the law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">By making the above submissions, the learned Advocate for the petitioners prays for making the Rule absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Per contra, Mr. Khurshedul Alam, the learned Deputy Attorney General (DAG) appearing for the State reads over the provisions of Section 526 of the CrPC and submits that the grounds taken by the accused-petitioners do not attract the provisions of Section 526 of the CrPC. He submits that there will be anarchy in the criminal justice administration of our country if trials of criminal cases are halted and transferred on these types of grounds. He contends that all the parties of this case, namely the accused persons and the witnesses, are the inhabitants of Jhenaidah, and submits that it would be harassment for them if the case is transferred to Dhaka or to any other district. He alleges that the attending facts amply suggest that this petition has been filed with an ill motive of delaying completion of the trial of this case. He further alleges that the Daily Prothom Alo, being a highly powerful newspaper of the country, has a tendency of influencing not only the social and political issues of the country, but also the judicial performance of this country and submits that if this case is transferred to Dhaka, a bad message will be passed on to the general litigants. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">By making the above submissions, the learned DAG humbly prays that the Rule should be discharged and, further, there should be a direction upon the trial Court to complete the trial of this case within a specified time.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">We have heard the learned Advocate for the petitioners and the learned DAG, perused the application together with its annexures wherefrom it transpires that the core issue for adjudication upon by this Court is whether there exists any reason for transferring this case from the present trial Court to any equivalent Court/Sessions Court in the District of Dhaka which may fall within the ambit of the provisions of Section 526(1) of the CrPC. For a fair adjudication of the issue, we may look at the provisions of Section 526(1) of the CrPC, which are reproduced below:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-indent: 27.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">526.(1) Whenever it is made to appear to the High Court Division:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27.5pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">that a fair and impartial inquiry or trial cannot be had in any Criminal Court subordinate thereto, or </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27.5pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">that some question of law of unusual difficulty is likely to arise, or</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27.5pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">that a view of the place in or near which any offence has been committed may be required for the satisfactory inquiry into or trial of the same, or </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27.5pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(d)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">that an order under this section will tend to the general convenience of the parties or witnesses, or </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 27.5pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(e)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">that such an order is expedient for the ends of justice, or is required by any provision of this Code; it may order-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 55pt; text-indent: -27.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(i)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">that any offence be inquired into or tried by any Court not empowered under sections 177 to 183 (both inclusive), but in other respects competent to inquire into or try such offence; </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 55pt; text-indent: -27.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(ii)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">that any particular case or appeal, or class of cases or appeals, be transferred from a Criminal Court subordinate to its authority to any other such Criminal Court of equal or superior; </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 55pt; text-indent: -27.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(iii)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">that any particular case or appeal be transferred to and tried before itself; or </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 55pt; text-indent: -27.5pt; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(iv)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">that an accused person be sent for trial to itself or to a Court of Sessions. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">From a plain reading of the above provisions, it appears that clauses (a) to (e) of sub-Section 1 of Section 526 of the CrPC are the grounds for entertaining an application under Section 526 of the CrPC and clauses (i) to (iv) of the same are the type, mode or nature of the orders that may be passed by this Court. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">While the grounds for transferring a case from the concerned trial Court to any other equivalent/superior Court are specifically spelt out in unambiguous wordings in clauses (a) to (d) of sub-Section 1 of Section 526 of the CrPC and, thus, the same being self-explanatory do not require any interpretation, however, clause (e) of the same having made a broader scope for the litigants to file an application for transferring a case from one Court to another Court on the ground/s which may appear to a party of a criminal case to be appropriate ‘for the ends of justice’, discussions on the meaning of the above expression and on the scope of its application sometimes becomes necessary. In other words, it becomes incumbent upon this Court to examine the claim of the applicant as to whether ‘for the ends of justice’, the case should to be transferred from the present trial Court to the any other competent Court and, thereby, see as to whether an order to that effect is expedient or not. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">When the learned Senior Advocate for the petitioners was faced with the question by this Court as to which ground/s of Section 526 of the CrPC calls for transferring this Court from the present trial Court to the District of Dhaka, he frankly conceded that clauses (a) to (d) of Section 526(1) do not attract the petitioners’ situation and put his best effort to make out his case within the provision of clause (e) of Section 526(1) of the CrPC. Let us now see what is meant by the above phraseology ‘for the ends of justice’ and, then, examine as to whether the facts and circumstances of this case demand transfer on the ground of ‘for the ends of justice’.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">It is not possible for any Court to define the expression ‘for the ends of justice’ in the fixed words and, thus, it would be an improper step for this Court to endeavour to lay down any guideline of the situations which may cover the said expression. Upon meticulously examining particular fact and circumstance of a case, when a Court arrives at a conclusion that there is no specific statutory provision in place which may fit in with the stated fact/circumstance for transferring the case from the concerned trial Court to a competent Court, but the conscience of a Judge, at the same<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>time, dictates to hold a view that the case should be transferred from the present trial Court to a competent Court for ensuring a fair trial, that situation may be called/termed to be a situation when this Court ‘for the ends of justice’ should pass necessary order/s for conducting the trial of the case either by the equivalent/superior Court of the same District or by the equivalent/superior Court of a different District or by the High Court Division itself. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In this case, the petitioners’ allegations are that this case has been filed at the instance of the Minister of the Ministry of Agriculture and, secondly, the learned Judge is not feeling comfortable to deal with the case. The petitioners of this case, however, have not been able to substantiate the above allegations by stating any plausible incident, not to speak of adducing any ocular evidence and, thus, these allegations appear to us to be vague. However, even if the allegations are taken to be true and, as per the prayer of the petitioners, the case is transferred to the District of Dhaka, the petitioners cannot guarantee that the same situation would not be created by the Minister in Dhaka; rather it would be convenient for the Minister to monitor the case and, thereby, influence the same. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">All that we wish to say that the Courts of Bangladesh are independent in dealing with any case and, if at any point of time, when a Judge is unduly communicated and pressured by the executive or by any person, the concerned trial Court Judge’s duty is either to deal with the matter by her/himself towards punishing the contemnor or to report the same to the Registrar of this Court. In this case, there is nothing in the order sheets (record) to show that the learned Judge of the trial Court has ever been communicated by any one requiring him to deal with the matter by himself or to report this Court about the alleged communication or pressure. With regard to the comments allegedly to have been made by the learned Judge, our observation is that, if the petitioner’s claim as to making the said comments is taken to be true, the learned Judge might have said it due to the non-cooperation of the accused-petitioners in completing the trial in the light of the fact that from the order sheets it is evident that the petitioners, instead of cross-examining the prosecution witnesses, not only have sought adjournments time and again, but also have eventually made prayer for transferring the case from his Court to another Court. Thus, it appears to us that the learned Judge might have said something at the instigation of the accused-petitioners. This Court, thus, does not find any materials/ evidence on record to blame the complainant for making the above comments, if it had at all happened. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Furthermore, from a perusal of the order sheets of this case, it transpires that the petitioners have sought adjournments on most of the dates and the delay has occurred in completing the trial. Therefore, the allegation raised by the learned Advocate for the petitioners that by making delay in completing the trial by the informant-side, they are being harassed - appears to us to be a false allegation.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The above discussions lead us to hold that the petitioner’s case does not come within the periphery of the provisions of Sections 526 of the CrPC and, hence, this Rule is destined to be discharged.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">      </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The power vested in the High Court Division by the provisions of Section 526(1) of the CrPC is discretionary in nature; meaning that if the High Court Division is satisfied that trial of a case should not be held in the present Court for securing ‘the ends of justice’ or for mitigating the situations set out in clauses (a) to (d) of Section 526(1) of the CrPC, then, this Court may pass necessary order/s to transfer it either to any equivalent criminal Court or to a Court of Sessions or to itself. Litigants must approach this Court/Sessions Judge with clean hands in availing the discretionary relief under Section 526 of the CrPC. In a fit and proper case, this Court shall never hesitate to transfer the trial of a case from the concerned Court to any competent Court for the sake of justice. At the same time, this Court owes a constitutional duty of maintaining a discipline in the administration of justice in the subordinate judiciary of this country. The propensity of the litigants to transfer the trial of a case from the concerned trial Court to another Court on omnibus ground requires to be trimmed down for the sake of administration of justice of this land and, which is why, the Legislature has empowered this Court to punish an applicant who intends to waste the invaluable time of this Court by filing trivial or fallacious application for transferring a case from the present Court to another Court. In this context, Section 526 (6A) of the CrPC may be looked at, which is reproduced below:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">526.
