(6A) Where any application for the exercise of the power conferred by this section is dismissed, the High Court Division may if it is of opinion that the application was frivolous or vexatious, order the applicant to pay by way of compensation to any person who has opposed the application such sum not exceeding one thousand taka as it may consider proper in the circumstances of the case.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">After hearing the learned Senior Advocate for the petitioner and the learned DAG at length, when it appeared to this Court that the Rule is devoid of any substance, we asked the learned Senior Advocate as to whether he intends to receive a detailed judgment on this case or he would non-prosecute the Rule to save this Court’s invaluable time which requires for delivering a full-fledged judgment. At that juncture, we were told by the learned Senior Counsel that the learned filing lawyer would inform this Court on the next day about receiving the full fledged judgment or non-prosecuting the Rule after consulting the matter with the petitioners. But unfortunately today, (on the next date of hearing the case) none appeared before this Court and, under the circumstance, this Court does not have any option other than to deliver a full-fledged judgment. Thus, it is a fit case to slap cost upon the petitioners under the provisions of Section 526(6A) of the CrPC. However, given the fact that Mr. Hassan Ariff, a Senior Advocate of this Court with a high standing in legal profession, was engaged in this case, we restrain ourselves from imposing any cost in discharging this Rule.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the result, the Rule is discharged without any order as to costs. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">However, the learned Judge of the trial Court of this case is directed to directly report henceforth to this Court, if he faces any pressure from any corner at any point of time in conducting the trial of the case. He is further directed to complete the trial of this case within the shortest possible time, preferably within thirty days, from the date of receipt of this judgment and order.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Office is directed to communicate this order at once to the learned Senior Judicial Magistrate, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Jhenaidah (Druta Bichar Adalat at Jhenaidah) by Fax and by registered post.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue%20__AUGUST_18(2)__Crl.%20Misc.%2047693%20of%2017__Muhammad%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarkar,%20J.__10.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. </span></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">47693 of 2017</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
652	<h2 class="blog_entry-title"> Azizur Rahman Vs.  Nur Alam and other, (Soumendra Sarker, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 4186 of 2014  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Soumendra Sarker, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Moloy Kumar Roy, Advocate ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ  </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Azizur Rahman </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Nur Alam and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Civil Procedure </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-01</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 346px;" width="431"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 187.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue%20__AUGUST__18(2)__C.%20R.%204186%20of%2014_Soumendra%20Sarker,%20J.__4.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 168.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Azizur Rahman</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">. . . Plaitniff-decree-holder-Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Nur Alam and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . Defendant-judgment-debtor--Opposite Parties</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Code of Civil Pro</span></strong></span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="color: #000000;">cedure (V of 1908)</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Order XXI</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Rule 29</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">A third party to the original suit/case have no <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">locus standi</em> to prefer such application for staying further proceedings of the Execution Case No. 12 of 2012 arising out of the judgment and final decree passed in Other Suit No.51 of 2006. Hence; the opposite </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">party No.13 was not at all lawfully authorized</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> to </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">bring any application for stay of the execution</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> case of a decree passed in the previous suit and the application under Order XXI, rule 29 of the Code of Civil Procedure was absolutely misconceived as it was not tenable in the eye of law.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">          </span>. . . (9 and 10)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">52 DLR 172; 56 DLR (AD) 139; 6 MLR (AD) 234</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr.</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Moloy Kumar Roy, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . For the petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Taj Mohammad Sheikh, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . For opposite party No. 13</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 24pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Soumendra Sarker, J:</span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> The Rule was issued calling upon the Opposite Party No.13 to show cause as to why the impugned judgment and order dated 17.06.2014, passed by the learned District Judge, Kurigram in Civil Revision No.18 of 2013 affirming the order dated 06.02.2013 passed by the learned Assistant Judge, Rajarhat, Kurigram in Other Execution Case No.12 of 2012 staying all further proceedings of the Execution Case till disposal of Other Suit No.05 of 2013, pending before the court of learned Assistant Judge, Rajarhat, Kurigram, filed by the opposite party No.13 as third party should not be set aside and/or pass such other or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The facts leading to the issuance of the Rule in a nutshell can be stated thus, that the present petitioner as plaintiff filed the original Partition Suit being No.51 of 2006 in the Court of learned Assistant Judge, Rajarhat, Kurigram. In that suit, the defendants No.2-7 and 9 after filing written statements contested the suit and after trial the learned trial court passed the judgment and decree on 14.01.2009 and 20.01.2009 respectively on contest against the contesting defendants and <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">ex parte</em> against the rest. Contesting defendant-opposite parties being aggrieved filed Other Appeal NO.32 of 2009 in the court of learned District Judge, Kurigram and the learned appellate court after hearing; affirmed the judgment and decree passed by the trial court by its judgment and decree dated 16.08.2011 and 21.08.2011 respectively. The trial court subsequently after receiving the report of the Advocate Commissioner along with filed book, sketch map, etc. drawn up the final decree on 23.08.2012 and the decree-holder-plaintiff-petitioner filed Execution Case No.12 of 2012 against the defendants to that case. In that execution case the present opposite party No.13 filed an application on 24.01.2013 under Order XLI, rule 29 of the Code of Civil Procedure for staying all further proceedings of Other Execution Case No.12 of 2012 till disposal of an Other Suit No.05 of 2013, pending before the court of learned Assistant Judge, Rajarhat, Kurigram filed by this opposite party No.13. The learned Assistant Judge on hearing the application allowed the same and stayed all further proceedings of the Execution Case No.12 of 2012 till disposal of the Other Suit No.05 of 2013 by his order dated 06.02.2013.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved the decree holder-petitioner preferred a Civil Revision being No.18 of 2013 in the Court of learned District Judge, Kurigram and the learned District Judge, Kurigram by the impugned judgment and order dated 17.06.2014 disallowed the revisional application and affirmed the order of the learned trial court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the impugned judgment and order of the learned 1<sup>st</sup> revisional Court the plaintiff-decree holder-petitioner have preferred this 2<sup>nd</sup> revisional application with leave of this Court under section 115(4) of the Code of Civil Procedure and obtained the Rule with an interim order of stay.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">During hearing of this Rule Mr. Moloy Kumar Roy, the learned Advocate appeared on behalf of the petitioner while Mr. Taj Mohammad Shaikh the learned Advocate appeared on behalf of the opposite party No.13.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the petitioner submits that the learned trial court as well as the 1<sup>st</sup> Court of revision during passing their judgment and orders committed gross illegality resulting in an error in the decision occasioning failure of justice in staying further proceedings of the Execution case filed by the plaintiff-decree holder-petitioner. The learned Advocate further submits that the opposite party No.13 is a third party to the original case and he has no <em><span style="mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal;">locus standi</span></em> to file any application for staying further proceedings of the execution case, but the learned trial court as well as the 1<sup>st</sup> revisional court without appreciation of law stayed the further proceedings of the execution case illegally. The learned Advocate also submits that during pendency of Execution Case No.12 of 2012 the present opposite party No.13 filed an application for staying further proceedings of the execution Case under Order XLI, rule 29 of the Code of Civil Procedure, which has no manner of application in that type of relief. The learned Advocate further submits that, admittedly the opposite party No.13 is a third party to the original suit and it’s subsequent execution case and for the said reason there was no scope to stay the proceedings of the execution case under the ambit of Order XLI, rule 29 of Code of Civil Procedure. The learned Advocate in support of his contention referred some decisions of this Court and our Apex Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">As against the aforesaid submissions of the learned Advocate for the petitioner the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the opposite party No.13 opposing the Rule submits that the civil revision under section 115(4) of the Code of Civil Procedure has a very limited scope and only for illegality and non-consideration of material facts and evidence on records resulting in an error in the decision occasioning failure of justice, a civil revision can be allowed and in the instant case; there is no such illegality and non-consideration of material facts or evidence resulting in an error in the decision occasioning failure of justice by which the impugned judgment and order can be interfered with. The learned Advocate after filing a counter affidavit on behalf of the opposite party No.13 further submits that at this stage inasmuch as a regular suit has been instituted by the opposite party No.13 being Other Suit No.5 of 2013 in respect of some land of the execution case, which is pending for disposal, the opposite party No.13 had locus standi to file the application for stay. The learned Advocate with regard to the scope of section 115 of the Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908) referred some decisions.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Considering the submissions of the learned Advocates having gone through the impugned judgment and order dated 17.06.2014 passed by the learned District Judge, Kurigram in Civil Revision No. 18 of 2013 along with the order of the trial court dated 06.02.2013 passed in Other Execution case No.12 of 2012 and all other relevant papers; it transpires that the present opposite party No.13 was not a party to the original Partition Suit No.51 of 2006 or it’s Other Appeal No.32 of 2009, or the Decree Execution Case No.12 of 2012. It further appears that the original Partition Suit being No. 51 of 2006 was decreed in favour of the decree holder-petitioner and during pendency of the execution case filed by the decree holder-petitioner, the present opposite party No.13 filed an application stating that he has filed a regular suit being Other Suit No.05 of 2013 in the Court of learned Assistant Judge, Rajarhat, Kurigram against the judgment and decree passed in Other Suit No.51 of 2006. In the pretext of citation of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Order XLI, rule 29 of the Code of Civil Procedure in the instant application for staying further proceedings of the execution case,the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the opposite party during his submission submits that, inadvertently instead of Order XXI, rule 29 of the Code of Civil Procedure wrongly, Order XLI was written in the application and it was a clerical mistake and for such mistake the client should not suffer due to the fault of his lawyer. However, treating the application under the provisions laid down in Order XXI, rule 29 of the Code of Civil Procedure, having gone through the contents of the application along with the judgment and order passed by the 1<sup>st</sup> Court of revision, I find that the learned District Judge, Kurigram during disposal of the revisional application filed before him under section 115(2) of the Code of Civil Procedure rightly opined that the plaintiff, who has filed the other Suit No.05 of 2013, Md. Moklesur Rahman in fact was not a party to the disposed of Other Suit No.51 of 2006, but obviously; the learned district judge wrongly held that<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>inasmuch as there is an apprehension of further complicacy, there is a necessity for staying further proceedings of the Decree Execution Case No.12 of 2012; prior to disposal of Other Suit No. 05 of 2013 which has been instituted against the judgment and final decree passed in Other Suit No.51 of 2006.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">           </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">From the plain reading of the provisions laid down in Rule 29 of Order XXI of the Code of Civil Procedure it is crystal much clear to draw such inference that the learned trial court as well as the 1<sup>st</sup> revisional court were totally misconceived in grasping the proposition of the relevant law. The fact remains that, a third party to the original suit/case have no <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">locus standi</em> to prefer such application for staying further proceedings of the Execution Case No.12 of 2012 arising out of the judgment and final decree passed in Other Suit No.51 of 2006. It is also a decided matter in our judicature. Hence, the petitioner being a third party to a decree has no legal character or lawful status to maintain an application for stay of the execution proceedings and pendency of a suit filed by third party is no ground for staying a proceedings of such execution case which has arise out of such a decree in which the applicant was not a party. Rule 29 of Order XXI of the Code of Civil Procedure; empowered only a party to a suit <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">viz.</span> the judgment-debtor and the decree holder for filing such application, and the court may stay execution of a decree until pendency of the suit which has been instituted by the judgment-debtor and not third party. [<em><span style="mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal;">Ref: 52 DLR 172; 56 DLR (AD) 139; 6 MLR (AD)234</span></em>.] </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Having regard to the facts, circumstances and the discussions along with the decisions referred to; I am constrained to hold such a view that admittedly the present opposite party No.13 was not a party to the suit, filed by the present petitioner who was plaintiff to the original suit being Other Suit No.51 of 2006, out of which the Other Execution Case No.12 of 2012 is pending.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Hence; the opposite party No.13 was not at all lawfully authorized to bring any application for stay of the execution case of a decree passed in the previous suit and the application under Order XXI, rule 29 of the Code of Civil Procedure was absolutely misconceived as it was not tenable in the eye of law. It had no manner of application in the instant of nature of case, but it appears that the learned court below on a total misconception and misapprehension of law stayed the proceedings of the Execution Case No.12 of 2012. The plaintiff to the subsequent suit being a stranger to the previous decree have got no legal character or <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">locus standi</em> to bring or maintain any such application for stay of the execution proceedings of the previous suit. Acordingly; the order recorded by the learned trial Judge, as well as the 1<sup>st</sup> Court of revision was illegal <em><span style="mso-bidi-font-family: Mangal;">ab initio</span></em>. Be that as it may; the impugned judgment and order passed by the learned District Judge, Kurigram upholding the order of the learned trial Judge in staying the execution proceedings of the Execution Case No 12 of 2012 suffers from illegality, legal infirmity and substantial error of law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the result; the Rule is made absolute. The impugned judgment and order dated 17.06.2014, passed by the learned District Judge, Kurigram in Civil Revision No.18 of 2013 affirming the order dated 06.02.2013 passed by the learned Assistant Judge, Rajarhat, Kurigram in Other Execution Case No.12 of 2012 staying all further proceedings of Other Execution Case till disposal of Other Suit No.05 of 2013, pending before the learned Assistant Judge, Rajarhat, Kurigram filed by the opposite party No.13 as third party is hereby set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The order of stay granted earlier at the time of issuance of the Rule stands vacated.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">However; there will be no order as to costs.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Communicate the judgment and order at once.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>Ed. <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue%20__AUGUST__18(2)__C.%20R.%204186%20of%2014_Soumendra%20Sarker,%20J.__4.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Revision No. </span></strong></a><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">4186 of 2014</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
653	<h2 class="blog_entry-title"> BBC Vs.  Registrar, Department of Patents and others, (Md. Ashraful kamal, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Trade Mark Appeal No. 02 of 2011  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Ashfaqul Islam, J And Md. Ashraful Kamal, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Syed Shahid Hossain, Advocate with Mr. Syed Imran Hossain, Advocate ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2014</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  British Broadcasting Corporation (BBC) </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Registrar, Department of Patents, Designs and Trade Marks, Trade Marks Registry Wing, Ministry of Industries, Government of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh and others.</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Trade Marks Act  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-01</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(SPECIAL STATUTORY JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; height: 330px; margin-right: auto;" width="641"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 283.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 330px;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -7.4pt 6.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Md. Ashfaqul Islam, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoHeading8" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -7.4pt 6.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">And</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in -7.4pt .0001pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Md. Ashraful Kamal, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> </strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">16.07.2014</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 53.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 330px;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue%20__AUGUST__18(2)__Trade%20Mark_%2002%20of%2011_Md.%20Ashraful%20Kamal,%20J.__5.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 256.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 330px;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">British Broadcasting Corporation (BBC)</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . Appellant </span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Registrar, Department of Patents, Designs and Trade Marks, Trade Marks Registry Wing, Ministry of Industries, Government of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh and others.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . Respondents</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Trade Marks Act (</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">XIX of 2009)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Sections 24 and 30</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 107%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%;">Section 30 of the Trade Marks Act, 2009 provides that priority of use of this mark gets paramount consideration compared to registration. The right created in favour of a registered proprietor of a trade mark is not an absolute right and is subservient to other provisions of the Act. In other words, registration of a trade mark does not provide a defence to the proceeding for passing of as under section 24 of the Act, 2009. A prior user of trade mark can maintain an action for passing off against any subsequent user of an identical trade mark including a registered user thereof. The right of good will and reputation in a trade mark was recognized at common law even before it was the subject of statutory law, prior to codification of trade mark law there was no provision in Bangladesh for registration of a trade mark. The right in a trade mark was acquired only by use thereof. This right has not been affected by the Act and is preserved and recognized by section 30. In the present case, it further appears from the record that there is absence of user of the trade of the respondents and that a trade mark which drops out of the use, dies when there are no goods which are offered for sale as there is no use of the trade mark. Apart from that, the respondents failed to appear before this Court with any affidavit-in-opposition and thereby<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>failed to show that they have carried on any business in the relevant class i.e. class 30 or have used the concerned trade </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">mark for the said business. In such a position,</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">we have no choice but to accept the averments</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%;"> and the claims that have been laid by the appellant.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">              </span>...(28 to 30, 35 and 36)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 105%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">Rolex Sa Vs. Alex Jewellery Pvt. Ltd &amp; Ors 2009 (41) PTC 284 (Del.); Smithkline Beecham PLC &amp; Anr. Vs. Sunil Sarmarkar &amp; ors, 2012 (132) DRJ 880; Allergran INC &amp; Anr. Vs. INTAS Pharmaceuticals, 2013 (53) PTC 36 (Del) and Rikhab Chand Jain &amp; Anr. Vs. T.T. Enterprises Pvt. Ltd. 2013 (54) PTC 489 (Del.) ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Mr. Syed Shahid Hossain, Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Syed Imran Hossain, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the appellant</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">No one appears</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . For the respondents</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27.35pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Md. Ashraful Kamal, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">This is an appeal under section 100 of the Trade Marks Act, 2009 presented on 28.02.2011 and the same was accepted on 01.03.2011 against the decision and order dated 15.07.2007 (communicated on 14.09.2010) passed by the Registrar of Trademarks, Dhaka rejecting the Trade Mark Application No. 49040 dated 14.11.1996 in Class-9 filed by the appellant for registration of the Mark BBC.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Short facts, necessary for the disposal of this appeal, are as follows;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">I.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The British Broadcasting Corporation (BBC) a public corporation incorporated and organized under the law of England and Wales by Royal Charter whose principal address is Broadcasting house, Portland Palace, London W1A<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>1AA, United Kingdom filed an application before the Registrar of Trademarks on 14.11.1996 for registration of the trade mark BBC being Application No. 49040 in class 9 in respect of sound, video and date recordings; films and sound films prepared for exhibition; carriers including records, discs, tapes, cassettes, cartridges and cards bearing or for use in bearing sound recordings, video recordings, data, images, games, graphics, text, programs or information; computer software; computer games; video games; electronic games; memory carriers; interactive compact discs; CD-ROMs; electrically, magnetically and optically recorded data for computers; instructional and teaching apparatus and instruments; sound, video and data recording and reproducing apparatus; games, apparatus for games and amusement apparatus all for use with or incorporating a television screen or <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">video monitor; coin of token operated electrical or</span> electronic amusement apparatus; loudspeakers; apparatus for use in recording, producing, presenting, broadcasting, transmitting, receiving, processing, reproducing, encoding and decoding of radio and television programmes, information and data; electrical and electronic broadcasting apparatus; parts and fittings for all the aforesaid goods; all other goods in class 9. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">II.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">After receiving the appellant’s trade mark application dated 14.11.1996, the respondent No.1 issued notice under section 14(1) of the Trade Marks Act, 1940 on 29.07.2004 upon the appellant to show cause as to why its application shall not be rejected under section 6(1)(e), 8(a) and 10(1) of the Trade Marks Act, 1940 for the reason of pendency of two marks namely application No. 9236 of Brown Boveri A.G. (BBC Products C/O Ramfry and son) and application No.37533 Bangladesh Brevy Centre (C/O Rajan Agency Dhaka).</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">III.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Thereafter, as per sub-rule (2) of the rule 24 of the Trade Marks Rules, 1963, the appellant on August 02, 2004 (within two months) sent his observations to the Trade Mark Registry, which was received by the respondent No.1’s office on 08.08.2004 vide memo No. 6474, the respondent No.1 on 30.04.2007 issued notice upon the appellant to appear before him on that date for hearing. Accordingly the appellant appeared on that date by giving hajira.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">IV.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">  </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">After that appellant filed an application before the respondent No.1(which was received by the respondent No.1 on 08.06.2008) requesting him for passing an early advertisement order for the process of registration of trade mark. Then on 08.02.2010 the appellant again filed an application before the respondent No.1 enquiring about his pending application.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">V.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Thereafter on 14.09.2010 the appellant filed another application before the respondent No.1 to inquire into the status of his trade mark. Then on 14.09.2010, the respondent No.1 informed the appellant that its application was rejected on 15.07.2007 and immediately on 20.09.2010 the appellant applied for the grounds of decision dated 15.07.2010 and the respondent No.1 supplied the said ground and decision on 01.11.2010.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved by the said orders dated 14.09.2010 and 01.11.2010 passed by the Registrar of Trademarks Dhaka in Trade Mark Application No. 49040 in Class-9 rejecting the application filed by the Appellant for registration of the Mark BBC, the appellant preferred this appeal under section 100 of the Trade Marks Act.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Syed Shahid Hossain alongwith Mr. Syed Imran Hossain, the learned Advocates appearing for the appellant, submits that the appellant’s mark BBC is in the use in Bangladesh territory earlier than Trade Marks No. 9236 and 37533. From Wikipdia, free Encyclopedia (page 13 supplementary paper Book) it is seen that Appellant uses and broadcast Bangla Program with the Trade Name BBC from 11.10.1941 whereas from the Trade Mark Journal (Page 14 and 15 of the supplementary paper book) it is evident that the use of the Trade Mark 9236 is from 26.04.1974 and that of the Trade Mark No. 37533 is after 20.04.1993.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He also submits that the appellant having Agreement at the same time with respondent No.3 i.e. owner of the Trade Mark 9236 since 19.10.1987 did not object to registration of the Trade Mark BBC of the appellant. So, there is no bar in registration of the appellant’s mark BBC as prayed for inspite of existence of the Trade Mark 9236 (Pg 01-08 of the supplementary paper Book). Moreover, the Respondent No.3 also issued a letter of Consent to the use and registration of the appellant’s trade mark BBC.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Therefore, the existing Mark 9236 does not create any bar to register the appellant’s mark BBC (pg 16 of the supplementary paper book)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He further submits that Trade Mark Application No. 37533 has no chance to be registered in view of already registered mark 9236 which is also earlier in use than the Mark 37533 and therefore cannot stand on the way of registration of the appellant’s mark who has co-existence Agreement with the mark 9236.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He also submits that the Appellant has co-existence Agreement with the owner of Registered Mark 9236 and also consent letter in respect of registration of the appellant’s mark BBC (P-16 of supplementary paper book) and the trade Mark application No. 37533 is actually abandoned.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Finally, Mr. Shahid submits that the appellant’s mark BBC as in use in Bangladesh since October 11, 1941 (pg 13 of the supplementary paper book) i.e. earlier to the mark 9236 which in use since 26.04.1974 and the mark 37533 which in use after 20.04.1993 (pg 14015 of the supplementary Paper Book) the appellant is entitled to registration as per section 30 of the Act 2009 as earlier user.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">No one appears for the respondents.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">We have gone through the Trade Mark Appeal alongwith the annexures annexed thereto, perused the record and considered the submissions made by the learned Advocate for the appellant.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It appears from the record that the respondent No.1 (the office of Trade Mark Registrar) on 29.07.2004 issued a notice under section 14(1) of the Trade Marks Act, 1940 upon the appellant to show cause as to why its application should not be rejected under section 6(1)(e), 8(a) and 10(1) of the Trade Marks Act, 1940 for the reason of pendency of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>two marks, namely, application No. 9236 of Brown Boveri A.G. (BBC Products C/O Ramfry and son) and application No. 37533 Bangladesh Brevy Centre (C/O Rajan Agency Dhaka). </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Thereafter, as per sub-rule (2) of rule 24 of the Trade Marks Rules, 1963, the appellant<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>on August 02, 2004 (within two months) sent his observation to the Trade Mark<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Registry, which was received by the respondent No.1’s office on 08.08.2004 vide memo No. 6474. line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">fl£rL<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">                            </span>H, Bl-1</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in;
