Maksud (Illegible) CO.</span></em></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .25in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>142/A, South Mirpur, Dhaka</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .25in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">Bf¢e/Bfe¡l Ef­l¡š² ¢ho­u ¢m¢Mai¡­h Efk¤š² Sh¡h fËc¡e L¢l­a f¡­le Abh¡ öe¡e£l fË¡bÑe¡ L¢l­a f¡¢l­hez BN¡j£ 3(¢ae) j¡­pl j­dÉ ¢m¢Mai¡­h Efk¤š² Sh¡h ¢c­a Abh¡ öe¡e£ c¡h£ L¢l­a hÉbÑ qC­m Bfe¡l/Bfe¡­cl B­hcefœ¢V f¢laÉš²/ fËaÉ¡MÉ¡a h¢mu¡ NZÉ qC­hz</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .25in; text-align: justify; text-indent: .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">ü¡rl/AØfø</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .25in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal;">f­r-®l¢SøÊÊ¡l, ®f­V¾V, ¢XS¡Ce J ®VÊX j¡LÑp A¢dcçl, Y¡L¡z</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">”</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">It is also admitted that though the appellant received the aforesaid notice dated 10.04.2007 duly, but failed to reply within the time mentioned in the said notice i.e. 3(three) months.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">Rule 22 to 25 of the Trade Marks Rules 1963 deals with “ <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u>PROCEDURE ON RECEIPT OF APPLICATION FOR REGISTRATION OF A TRADE MARK” , </u></strong>which runs thus;<u></u></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 1.0in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Rule 22-<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u> Acknowledgment of receipt of application.</u></strong> Every application for the registration of a trade mark in respect of any goods shall, on receipt, be acknowledged by the Registrar.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 1.0in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">Rule 23- <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u>Search</u></strong>. Upon receipt of an application for the registration of a trade mark in respect of any goods the Registrar shall cause a search to the made amongst the registered marks and amongst the pending applications for the purpose of ascertaining whether there are on record in respect of the same goods or description of goods any marks identical with the mark sought to be registered or so nearly resembling it as to deceive or cause confusion and the Registrar may cause the search to be renewed at any time before the acceptance of the application, but shall not be bound to do so.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 1.0in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Rules24-<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u>objection to acceptance</u></strong></span></em><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;"> -Hearing</span></u></em></strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">. (1) If, on consideration of the application, and of any evidence of use or of distinctiveness or of any other matter which the applicant may or may be required to furnish the Registrar has any objection to the acceptance of the application or proposes to accept it subject to such conditions, amendments, disclaimers, modifications or limitations as he may think right to impose, the Registrar shall communicate such objection or proposal in writing to the applicant.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 1.0in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">(2) Unless within 2(two) months from the date of the communication mentioned in sub-rule(1), the applicant alters his application according to the proposal aforesaid, or sends his observations to the Trade Marks Registry or applies for a hearing, the application shall be deemed to have been abandoned and no further reference to the applicant shall be necessary.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 1.0in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">(3) An application which is treated as abandoned under sub-rule (2) or sub-section (3) of section 16 may be restored 3[within two months] to file on sufficient cause being shown to the satisfaction of the Registrar and on an application to that effect being made in Form TM-56 accompanied by a statement of the case.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 1.0in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">Rule 25-<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u>Decision of Registrar</u></strong>. (1) The decision of the Registrar at a hearing under rule 24 or without a hearing if the applicant has duly communicated his observations in writing, and has stated that he does not desire to be heard, shall be communicated to the applicant in writing, and if the applicant intends to appeal from such decision he may within one month from the date of such communication apply on Form TM-15 to the Registrar requiring him to state in writing the grounds of and the materials used by him in arriving at, his decision.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 1.0in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">(2) In a case where the Registrar makes any requirements to which the applicant does not object, the applicant shall comply therewith before the Registrar issues a statement in writing under sub-rule(1).</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">(3) The date when such statement is sent shall be deemed to be the date of the Registrar’s decision for the purpose of appeal.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">In the present case, it is evident from the record that the Registrar after receipt of the petitioner’s application dated 14.03.2005 for the registration of the Trade Mark ‘RANI’ made search as per Rule 23 and then issued notice under section 14(1) of the Trade Marks Act, 1940 read with Rule 24(1) of the Trade Marks Rules, 1963.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">If an applicant in response to a notice issued upon him under Section 14(1) of the Trade Marks Act, 1940 read with Rule 24(1) of the revised trade Marks Rules, 1963 does not take any steps, the Registrar under Rule 24(2) shall treat the application as abandoned after the expiry of 90 days from the date of receipt of the notice.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">In the present case, the petitioner after receipt of the notice under Section 14(1) of the Trade Mark Act, 1940<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>did not send his observations in writing to the Trade Marks Registry as per sub rule-2 of Rule 24 nor he has stated that he applied for a hearing and as such it becomes clear that the application must be deemed to have been abandoned and no further reference/communication to the applicant shall be necessary.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">The Rule is procedural no doubt, but is mandatory and non-compliance of the same renders the application to be treated as abandoned as provided by sub rule (2) of Rule 24 of the Revised Trade Marks Rules, 1963. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Therefore, it has been held that non-compliance with the sub rule (2) of Rule 24 of the Revised Trade Marks Rules, 1963 will lead to the inference that the applicant of the application dated 14.03.2005 (appellant) has nothing to say in rebuttal against the said notice dated 10.04.2007 under Section 14(1) of the Trade Marks Act, 1940<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>sent by the Registrar.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Since no observation sent or application made for hearing either within the time mentioned in the notice or in the prescribed manner, the inference would be that the same have been waived. </span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">32.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">When any such application became abandoned for non compliance of sub rule (2) of Rule 24, then the applicant can restore his application by filing application as per Rule 24(3), which is for restoration of the said abandonment being made in Form TM-56 accompanied by a statement of the case. The intention of the legislature was to give further opportunity to the applicant, whose, application was so abandoned for non compliance of section 16(3) or Rule 24(2). But this has not been done here. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">33.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Despite the fact, that as per Rule 76, the Registrar has the discretion to extend time in taking any steps by any party before him and in the present case the appellant could take advantage of that Rule by filing TM55 praying for condonation of delay in filling such restoration application in time but they have not done so. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">34.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Therefore, the application of the predecessor of the appellant was abandoned on 16.07.2007, after expiry of the three months from the date of show cause notice dated 10.04.2007.  Thus the Registrar rightly proceeded with the application filed by the respondent No. 2.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">35.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Moreover, the appellant did not come before this Court with clean hands. Because, in the paragraph 4 of this Trade Mark Application, appellant has stated that the predecessor of the appellant (Md. Babar Chaklader) had been manufacturing, marketing and    selling ‘Spices’ with trade mark word ‘RANI’ since 2004. But in the application dated 14.03.2005, Babul Chaklader himself stated that the mark is being used since March, 2005.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">36.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Despite the fact the power of attorney by declaration of affidavit before the Notary Public, Dhaka dated 20.08.2009 (Annexure-1) and the deed of assignment dated 24.08.2009 (Annexure-2) are self contradictory and the Annexure-1 and 2 clearly proved the fraudulent acts of the appellant. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">37.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">On the conspectus of the observations as made above the inevitable result that follows is that this appeal fails.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">38.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">In the result, the appeal is dismissed. The order dated 05.07.2011 passed by the respondent No.1 Registrar is hereby upheld.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">39.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Communicate this judgment and order at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>Ed.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></strong></p></div></div></div>
655	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Eastern Builders Ltd. and other Vs.  Bangladesh and others, (Md. Nuruzzaman, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 4838 of 2011  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Nuruzzaman, J And S. H. Md. Nurul Huda Jaigirdar, J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. A.B.M. Bayezid, Advocate,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ  </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  M/S. Eastern Builders Ltd. Represented by its Managing    Director, A.B.M. Mortoza being dead- Anowara Begum having its register office </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Bangladesh, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of  Post, Telegraph and Telecommunication, 3rd Floor, Saptom Building, Bangladesh Secretariat, Dhaka and others. </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Civil Procedure </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-01</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 1126px;" width="594"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 245.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Md. line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 261.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="tab-stops: 333.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; Petitioner</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; tab-stops: 333.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="tab-stops: 333.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Bangladesh</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Post, Telegraph and Telecommunication, 3<sup>rd</sup> Floor, Saptom Building, Bangladesh Secretariat, Dhaka and others.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; tab-stops: 333.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . </span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Opposite Parties</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; tab-stops: 333.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(In <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">C. R. 4838 of 2011</span></span></em></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; tab-stops: 333.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">With</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="tab-stops: 333.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Bangladesh</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Post, Telegraph and Telecommunication, 3<sup>rd</sup> Floor, Saptom Building, Bangladesh Secretariat, Dhaka and others.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; tab-stops: 333.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . R. 365 of 2012)</span></u></em></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 38</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Executing Court cannot calculate the interest in the instant Execution Case in violation the dictum of the appellate Court as decided earlier occasion up to Hon’ble Appellate Division of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh. Moreso, it is well settled maxim of law as enunciated by the apex Court that the Executing Court cannot go beyond the decree.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                         </span>. . . (34)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">M/s A.Z. company, Karachi Vs. R. No. 365 of 2012)</span></em></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Dr. Shahdeen Malik, Advocate with </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Mr.</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> Md.</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> Monjur Alam, Advocate.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .<u>For the petitioner No. 3</u> </span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(In C. R. No. 365 of 2012)</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Mr. A.B.M Bayezid, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . . <u>For the opposite party</u> </span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; text-align: justify;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(In C. R. No. 365 of 2012)</span></em></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Md. Nuruzzaman, J:</span></u></strong> <span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">These two Rules were issued calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why the impugned judgment and order No. 61 dated 27.09.11, order No. 65 dated 02.11.2011 and order No. 66 dated 27.11.2011 passed by learned Joint District Judge, 3<sup>rd</sup> Court, Dhaka in Money Execution Case No. 11 of 2001 arising out of Money Suit No. 13 of 1986 should not be set aside and /or such other or further order or orders passed as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The Civil revision No. 4838 of 2011 arose on application at the instance of M/S Eastern Builders against order No. 65 dated 02.11.11 and order No. 66 dated 27.11.2011. The Civil Revision No. 365 of 2012 arose on an application at the instance of Government of Bangladesh and others against the order No. 61 dated 27.09.2011 and order No. 67 dated 16.01.2012.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">This Bench simultaneously heard both the revisional applications being arises from the same execution case and impugned orders were passed by the same Court. Therefore, we are of the opinion that by a single judgment <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">both the revisional applications should be disposed</span> of, otherwise, there are every possibility of conflicting findings and decisions. However, both the Civil Revisions would be governed by the result of this single judgment.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The material facts, relevant for disposal of the instant Rule, in short, are that the petitioner as plaintiff on 22.01.1986 instituted Money suit No. 13 of 1986 in the Court of Subordinate Judge, Dhaka for realization of Tk. 60,40,551.71 ( sixty lac forty thousand five hundred fifty one taka and seventy one poisha) contending, inter alia, that the plaintiff is the private Limited company. It has been carrying business of contractor, builders, manufactures, Engineering etc. The plaintiff company is the government approved first class contractor under the public works department of the Government of Bangladesh. The postal department of the government invited tender from first class contractors for construction of 12 storied building for the office of the Director General, Bangladesh post office and General Manager, Post life insurance at 17, Dilkusha Commercial area, Dhaka. The plaintiff company submitted tender and became the lowest bidder. The Director General Bangladesh post office accepted the lowest offer of the plaintiff company. On 23.10.1980 an agreement was executed and signed between the plaintiff and the Director (running) General Bangladesh Post office. The period of 18 months time were allowed for completion of the above mention work. The Director of planning on 01.02.1983 wrote a letter to the plaintiff requesting him to hand over the side to the executive Engineer enclosing a copy of letter dated 29.05.1982 which read as follow:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>“The period of 18 months allowed for completion of the above mention work expired on 22.04.1982. Contract agreement dated 23.10.1980 made with you have become void and thereafter forfeited the earnest and security money of the plaintiff company.” </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Hence, the plaintiff company had been compelled to file a suit for realization of Tk. 60,40,551.71 ( sixty lac forty thousand five hundred fifty one taka and seventy one poisha)<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>as liquidated damage. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Money Suit No. 13 of 1986 was decreed on 21.01.2001 decreeing Tk. 60,40,551.75 (sixty lac forty thousand five hundred fifty one taka and seventy five poisha) ”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Feeling aggrieved by the impugned judgment and decree dated 21.01.2001 preferred the First Appeal being No. 245 of 2002. A Division Bench of this Division heard the First Appeal No. 245 of 2002 and dismissed the appeal with modification by its judgment dated 6 and 9 July 2006. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The judgment debtor preferred the Civil petition for leave to appeal being No. 522 of 2007 before the Hon’ble Appellate Division which was dismissed as barred by limitation by order dated 22.07.2008. The judgment debtor unsuccessfully filed review petition 130 of 2009 which was also dismissed by the Appellate Division on 03.01.2010.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Hence, Money Decree Execution case No. 11 of 2001 was proceeded in accordance with law at the instance of the decree holder. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">While the Money Decree Execution Case No. 11 of 2001 was so pending, the decree holder filed an application praying for direction upon the judgment debtor to pay the amount of the decree holder as calculated herein above till 13.09.2011. In view of the application dated 22.09.2011 the Executing Court by its order No. 61 dated 27.9.2011 directed the judgment debtor to pay tk. 23,99,23,660.06 (twenty three crore, ninety nine lac, twenty three thousand, six hundred sixty taka and<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>zero six poisha).</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The judgment debtor on 27.10.2011 filed an application under section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure for stay the operation of the order dated 27.9.2011 with a prayer to re hear the aforesaid application. The learned Joint District Judge, 3<sup>rd</sup> Court by its order No. 65 dated 02.11.2011 stayed the operation of the order No. 61 dated 27.11.2011. Hence, at the instance of decree holder the instant Rule being Civil Revision No. 48305 of 2011.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">On contra, the judgment debtor filed the revisional application against the order No. 67 dated 16.01.2012 passed by Joint District Judge, 3<sup>rd</sup> Court, in Money Execution Case No. 11 of 2001 arising out of Money Suit No. 13 of 1986 directing the judgment debtor to pay Tk. 23,99,23,666.06/- as per order No. 61 passed on 17.09.2011</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The opposite parties contested in both the Rules by filing an counter affidavit respectively, in revision No. 365 of 2012 a supplementary affidavit and counter affidavit were submitted by the opposite parties stating, inter alia, that the decree holder got decree in the Money suit No. 13 of 1986 against which the defendants preferred the First appeal being No. 245 of 2002 in the High Court Division of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh. A Division Bench of the High Court Division affirmed the judgment and decree with modification by its judgment dated 6 and 9 July 2006. The judgment debtor against the judgment of the High Court Division dated 6 and 9 July 2006 preferred Civil Petition for leave to appeal No. 522 of 2007 which was dismissed on 22.07.2007. Thereafter, they filed the review application which was also dismissed. It has been stated in the counter affidavit that the calculation sheet in respect of the realization of the money is not relevant and necessary as the High Court Division on earlier occasion directed the judgment debtor to make payment as modified in the judgment of First Appeal No. 245 of 2002. Therefore, the decree holder has no locus standi who filed an application calculating the facts and figure beyond the decree Thus, the Executing Court accepting such calculation committed error of law violating the direction of the High Court Division passed in First Appeal No. 245 of 2002, as such, the order No. 61 dated 27.9.2011 is liable to be set aside. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The opposite party No. 3 also of Civil Revision No. 365 of 2012 filed 2 supplementary affidavit in 2<sup>nd</sup> supplementary affidavit dated 07.01.2018<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>stated as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>It is stated that during pendency of the Civil Revision No. 4838 of 2011 and Civil Revision No. 365 of 2012 in the Hon’ble High Court Division, a cheque has been presented by the Opposite parties (Bangladesh, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Post, Telegraph and Telephone and others) in accordance with the judgment and decree dated 6<sup>th</sup> and 9<sup>th</sup> July, 2006 passed in First Appeal No. 245 of 2002 passed by the Hon’ble High Court Division of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh, being Cheque No. </span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-ansi-language: EN;">N 2102267 </span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">dated 03.01.2018 amounting to Taka 43,08,293.34 (forty three lac eight thousand two hundred ninety three taka and thirty four paisa) in favour of M/S Eastern Builders Ltd. Accordingly, the payee of the said cheque, M/S Eastern Builders Ltd. has been notified to collect the said cheque from the concerned office through an office order being Memo No. </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-ansi-language: EN;">¢f¢h/4-25/83/f¡VÑ-5</span></strong> <span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">dated 03.01.2018 by registered post to its address at 47, Dilkusha Commercial Area, Dhaka-1000. However, after observing the necessary official formalities, including displaying the notice at a visible place of the addressee (</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-ansi-language: EN;">mVL¡Cu¡ S¡l£</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">)<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>but the said letter containing Memo No.</span> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-ansi-language: EN;">¢f¢h/4-25/83/f¡VÑ-5</span></strong> <span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>dated<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>03.01.2018 was returned to the office of the opposite parties (Bangladesh, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of post, Telegraph and Telephone and others) as undelivered, and till now nobody has come forward to collect it. Under the circumstances, the Cheque No. </span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>N 2102267 </span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">dated 03001.2018 amounting to Taka 43,08,293.34 (Forty three lac eight thousand two hundred ninety three taka and thirty four paisa) in favour of M/S Eastern Builders Ltd. has been submitted before the Hon’ble Court which is now kept in the custody of the Hon’ble Court as Cheque No.</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> N 2102267<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">dated 03.01.2018 amounting to taka 43,08,293.34 (Forty three lac eight thousand two hundred ninety three taka and thirty four paisa) in favour of M/S Eastern Builders Ltd. as (Annexure-II) which has been annexed with the 1<sup>st</sup> supplementary affidavit.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The petitioner denying the contents of the counter affidavit first and 2<sup>nd</sup> supplementary of the opposite party No. 3 filed counter reply. Mr. A.B.M Bayejid, the learned Advocate for the petitioner has submitted that in view of the order dated 27.09.2011 an application was filed by the judgment debtor on 03.07.2011 for ascertaining the amount to be paid to the decree holder in accordance with<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the Judgment passed by the High Court Division passed in F.A No. 245 of 2002, stating that, nothing is left over to the executing Court to decide the matter afresh and thus, committed serious error of law in the decision in staying the operation of the order dated 27.09.2011. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The Court below became fauctus officio and he cannot pass such order affecting the earlier order which is liable to be set aside by this Hon’ble Court. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">There is no provision of law to file objection by the judgment debtor before in the executing Court because section 47 was omitted in the year 1983 and the judgment debtor cannot file any objection in an execution case and, as such, the order passed on 02.11.2011 and the order passed on 27.11.2011 are not tenable in law and both the orders are liable to be set aside for the ends of justice. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Moshaffor Hossain Sarder, D.A.G with Mr. S. Rashed Jahangir, D.A.G appearing on behalf of the opposite party No. 1 has submitted that the executing Court accepting the calculation has committed serious error of law beyond the judgment passed by the High Court Division in First Appeal No. 245 of 2002 and, as such, the impugned order is liable to be set aside. He took us through the exhibit 3 a judgment passed by a Division Bench of this Division in First Appeal No. 245 of 2002 and specifically drawn up our attention in the discussion and decision which are as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">“From the above discussion the moot question is whether the plaintiff entitled to the relief claimed. We have already found that the plaintiff has invested huge amount in construction of the said project and the plaintiff could not be able to proceed with the further construction due to the fault of the Engineer and Officials of the Defendants. Earlier one M/s Create Constructions Limited also removed. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">From the plaint it appears that the plaintiff claimed the money including interest as stated in the schedule of the plaint. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Under section 73 of the Contract Act we find that the plaintiff is not entitled to the interest as stated No. 3 of the schedule of the plaint on the aforesaid investment amounting to Taka 33,25,670.00 at the rate of 15% per annum for 3 years. It has been held in he case of M/s A.Z. Company, Karachi Vs. Messers S.Kaula Bukhsh Muhammad Bashir, Karachi reported<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>in 17 DLR (SC)-404 that the award of interest generally not payable for damages for breach of contract. If it is not specifically made in the contract. It has been held in the case of M/s Amin Jute Mills Ltd. Vs. A.R.N.G reported in 28 DLR(AD)-76 that Section 73 of the Contract Act says that the loss or damages towards compensation may be claimed in the event of breach. The plaintiff may recover the loss and damages for the breach of contract and defaulting party must pay the loss and damages and compensation and their earnest money amounting to Taka 1,25,670/= value of the materials and cost of actual work done 32,000/= and compensation for loss of profit @ 15% of Tender amount of Taka 65,50,822.25 which amounting to Taka 9,82,623.34.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Since we have already found that the loss and damages caused due to fault of the Defendant-Appellant the penalty imposed upon the plaintiff are not sustainable in law and the plaintiff committed no fault and penal action cannot be imposed upon the plaintiff. The judgment and decree passed by the trial Court is hereby upheld with the modification that the plaintiff is not entitled to any interest upon the invested<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>amount of Taka 17,32,258.37.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The appeal, is therefore, dismissed with the above modification. The contesting Defendant-Appellants are hereby directed to pay the plaintiff decreetal amount except the interest as claimed by the plaintiff within 6 months from the date of decree failing which <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the plaintiff-Respondents are at liberty to realize</span> the amount in due process of the Court.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In support of his submissions he cited the decision reported in 15 BLD (AD)-51, 42-DLR (AD)-294, AIR-1987-Patha-133.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">We have anxiously considered the submissions advanced by the learned Advocates of the respective parties. The instant revisional applications arises challenging the legality and propriety of order No. 65 dated 02.11.2011 and order No. 66 dated 27.11.2011 passed by Joint District Judge, 3<sup>rd</sup> Court in Money Decree Execution Case No. 11 of 2001 and thereby staying the operation of order No. 61 dated 27.09.2011.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The moot question before us whether the learned Joint District Judge in passing the impugned order No. 65 dated 27.11.2011 and impugned order No. 66 dated 27.11.2011 are justified in view of judgment and decree passed in money suit No. 13 of 1986 which was modified by this Division in First Appeal No. 245 of 2002.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Considering the facts and circumstances and judgment dated 21.01.2001 passed in money suit No. 13 of 1986 and judgment and decree passed in First Appeal No. 245 of 2002 it is clearly divulged<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>that on the earlier occasion the judgment of the trial Court has been affirmed by the High Court Division with modification which has been tested before the appellate Division including review application however, the Judgment dated 6 and 9 July 2006 passed by the High Court Division was upheld by the appellate Division. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">From the materials on record of Money Decree Execution case No. 11 of 2001 it appears that the present dispute has been arisen from the order No. 61 dated 29.09.2011 wherein the Executing Court on an application of the decree holder fixed the realisable money from the judgment debtor amounting Tk. 23,99,23660.06 (twenty three crore, ninety nine lac, twenty three thousand, six hundred sixty taka and zero six poisha). The judgment debtor against the said order preferred another revisional application being Civil Revision No. 365 of 2012 wherein they prayed for setting aside the impugned order No. 61 dated 27.09.2011 and order No. 67 dated 16.01.2012 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, 3<sup>rd</sup> Court, Dhaka in Money Decree Execution case No. 11 of 2001 arising out of money suit No. 13 of 1986 wherein Court directed the judgment debtor to pay Tk. 23,99,23660.06 (twenty three crore ninety nine lac twenty three thousand six hundred sixty taka and zero six poisha).</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The facts as has been derived from the revisional application being No. 365 of 2012 it is revealed that facts are same and parties are also same. So, we are not inclined to reiterate the same facts once again. The grounds set forth in the revisional application and submissions advanced by the learned Advocates of the respective parties and narrative of the counter affidavits it is clearly manifested that both the parties are litigating from 1986. However, the litigation although ended once up to the appellate Division but it has started again through Money Execution<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Case No. 11 of 2001.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In the mean time Mr. A.B.M Mortuza, the managing Director of the company M/s Eastern Builders Ltd. died in the year 2009. But unfortunately till now dispute has not been resolved paying the deecrital amount.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mr. Jahanigr Rashed, the learned D.A.G appearing in the revisional application No. 365 of 2012 has submitted that the Executing Court committed an error of law resulting in an error in the decision in passing the order dated 16.01.2012 directing the judgment debtor pay the amount of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Tk. 23,99,23,666.06 on 20.02.2012 which clearly occasioned failure of justice.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">As the execution court was pleased to fix <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the matter on 23.02.2011 for taking further hearing</span> of the parties for proper calculation but the same court without going to that point passed the impugned judgment order No. 61 dated 27.09.2011<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and subsequently order No. 67 dated 16.01.2012 and, as such, committed an <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">error in the decision occasioning failure of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>justice.</span> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">As the Executing Court allowed the petitioner to file written objection against the re calculation of the amount and the matter was fixed on 20.02.12<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>for holding hearing but in the meantime the opposite party came to the Hon’ble High Court Division and file Civil Revision No. 4838 of 2011 and obtained the order of stay for 2(two) months and, as such, the petitioner have been deprived form getting chance of hearing and, as such, an opportunity or scope may kindly be given to the petitioner by the Hon’ble Court to place his case for ends of justice because on earlier occasion the High Court Division in First Appeal No. 245 of 2002 on hearing both the sides modified the decree of the trial Court holding that the plaintiff is entitled to a decree for the security amount of Tk. 1,25,670/- and for the amount of works done accordingly to Tk. 32,00,000 and profit of Tk. 9,82,623.34 which is in total comes to 43,08293.34 but the Executing Court committed an error of law in the decision occasioning failure of justice in passing the order to pay Tk. 23,99,23,666.66 to the plaintiff decree holder without complying the dictum of the High Court Division. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The Executing Court committed an error of law in the decision occasioning failure of justice in allowing interest as claimed by the decree holder ignoring the judgment and decree passed by the High Court Division in First Appeal No. 245 of 2002.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The Executing Court erred in law in passing the decision occasioning failure of justice in holding that the judgment debtor has not filed any written objection against the claim of the amount and also against the re calculation of the amount at the instance of the decree holder.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">We have considered the submissions of the learned Advocates appearing for the respective parties in both the revisional applications and grounds set forth therein. We are of the view that the judgment and decree passed by this Division in First Appeal No. 245 of 2002 is binding upon both the parties as well as the Executing Court. However, we find that in the Execution Case the learned Judge by his order No. 61 dated 27.09.2011 accept the calculation submitted by the decree holder and thereby directed to pay the Tk. 23,99,23660.06 (twenty three crore, ninety nine lac, twenty three thousand, six hundred sixty taka and zero six poisha) from which the instant two revisional applications had arose.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">We have perused and considered the application dated 11.07.2010 by dint of which the trial Court fixed the amount of tk. 23,99,23660.06 (twenty three crore, ninety nine lac, twenty three thousand, six hundred sixty taka and zero six poisha) it has been contended by Mr. A.B.M Bayejid, the learned Advocate for the petitioner in Civil Revision No. 4838 of 2011 that on earlier occasion the opposite party No. 3 on an application withdraw the amount as order passed by the Court below agreeing to deposit Tk. 10,46,49,977.55 (ten crore, forty six lac, forty nine thousand, nine hundred seventy seven taka and fifty five poisha). So, according by Mr. Bayejid, the learned Advocate for the opposite party pointed that the opposite party No. 3 admitted the claim of the petitioner up to Tk. 10 crore and odds. Now they cannot deny such admission. The submission advanced by Mr. Bayejid in respect of Tk. 10 crore admitting by the opposite party No. 3 does not seem us convincing rather, it appears that the Court modified the order of attachment directing the opposite party No. 3 for keeping deposit Tk. 10 Crore and odds they can operate the bank account. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">33.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Now, we are to decide whether the application for calculation of money by the decree holder whether justified in view of the judgment of the High Court Division passed in First Appeal No. 245 of 2001. We have gone through the judgment dated 6 and 9 January, 2001 wherefrom it is crystal clear that their lordships decided the facts and law in the earlier occasion at the time disposal of the above mentioned First<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Appeal. In view of precedent to the case of M/s A.Z. company, Karachi Vs. M/s S. Kaula Baksha Muhammad Bashir Karachi<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>reported in 17 DLR (S.C) 404 and M/S Amin Jute Mills Ltd.Vs ARNG reported<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>in 28 DLR (AD)-76 wherein it has been settled that in view of provision of section 73 of the contract Act the appeal was allowed in part modifying the judgment of the trial Court which are as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27.35pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">“The judgment and decree passed by the trial Court is hereby upheld with the modification that the plaintiff is not entitled to any interest upon the invested amount of Taka 17,32,258.37(seventeen lac, thirty two thousand, two hundred fifty eight and thirty seven poisha).</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The appeal is therefore dismissed with the above modification. the contesting Defendant-Appellants are hereby directed to pay the plaintiff the decreetal amount except the interest as claimed by the plaintiff within 6 months from the date of decree failing which the plaintiff –respondents are at liberty to realize the amount in due process of the Court.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">34.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Therefore, we find that the impugned order No. 61 dated 27.09.2011 cannot be sustained in law as the calculation given by the decree holder is extraneous and superfluous as well as beyond the decree. We are of the considered view that the Executing Court cannot calculate the interest in the instant Execution Case in violation the dictum of the appellate Court as decided earlier occasion up to Hon’ble Appellate Division of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh. More so, it is well settle maxim of law as enunciated by the apex Court that the Executing Court cannot go beyond the decree. So, in calculating the interest in the instant Execution Case the Executing Court committed an error occasioning failure of justice. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">35.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Therefore, we find merit in the Rule of Civil Revision No. 365 of 2012.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">36.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In the result the Rule is made absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">37.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">On contra, in the above facts and circumstance and discussions made hereinabove we are of the considered view that the claim as calculated by the petitioner in Execution Case and claimed in the Civil Revision No. 4838 of 2011 cannot be sustained in law. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">38.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Thus, the Rule of Civil Revision No. 4838 of 2011 bears no merit. </span></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">39.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt;
