mso-ansi-language: EN;">In the result, the Rule of Civil Revision No. 4838 of 2011 is discharged. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">40.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The order of stay granted earlier is hereby recalled and shall stand vacated.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">41.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">However, the opposite party No. 3 by supplementary affidavit deposited the cheque of an amount of Tk. 43,08,293.34 (forty three lac, eight thousand two hundred ninety three taka and thirty four poisha) according to the judgment of the High Court Division passed in First Appeal No. 245 of 2011 admitting the judgment in favour of the Eastern Builders Ltd. The opposite party company M/S Eastern Builders Ltd. of Civil Revision No. 365 of 2012 will be entitled to encash the above cheque bearing No. </span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-ansi-language: EN;">N </span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">2103017 dated 11.4.2018 through current Account No. <strong>105 </strong>(20503110100010517) lying with Islami Bank Bangladesh Ltd., Motijheel Branch, Dhaka. However, the Manager of the Bank is directed to allow the encashment of the cheque of the money after ascertaining the identity of the legally constituted Managing Director as per provision of Company Act. It may be mentioned here that cheque number is corrected vide order dated 12.4.2018.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">42.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The office is directed to send the cheque to the Executing Court for taking necessary step at once without any delay. The Executing Court is further directed to deposit the cheque No.</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> N </span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">2103017 dated 11.4.2018 in the aforementioned account of Islami Bank Bangladesh Limited, Motijheel Branch, Dhaka forthwith on receipt of this judgment. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">43.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Office is directed to communicate the judgment at once to the Executing Court. The Executing Court is directed to send a attested photo copy of the judgment to the Manager, Islami Bank, Bangladesh Limited Motijheel Branch for necessary action</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">  </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">         Ed.  </span></strong></p><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue%20__AUGUST__18(2)__C.%20R.%204838%20of%2011_Md.%20Nuruzzaman,%20J.__6.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Revision No. </span></strong></a><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">4838 of 2011</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
656	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Hafizuddin Vs. Mozaffor Mridha, (Hasan Foez Siddique, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL APPEAL NO. 552 OF 2009  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J Muhammad Imman Ali, J Hasan Foez Siddique, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Syed Amirul Islam, Senior Advocate, instructed by Syed Mahbubar Rahman, Advocate-on-Record.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ   ( AD) </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2017</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Hafizuddin  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Mozaffor Mridha being dead his heirs 1. Asia Begum and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Waqf Ordinance </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-01</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CIVIL)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; height: 236px; margin-right: auto;" width="650"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes; height: 112.85pt;"><td style="width: 264.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Muhammad Imman Ali, J</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">17.08.2017</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 45.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue__AUGUST_%2018(2)__C.%20A.552%20of%2009__Hasan%20Foez%20Siddique,%20J._AD__4_.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 292.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Md. Hafizuddin </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">--- <u>Appellant</u></span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">=Versus=</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mozaffor Mridha being dead his heirs 1. Asia Begum and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">--<u>Respondents</u></span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Waqf Ordin</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">ance (I of 1962) </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 2 </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Three basic principles governed the waqf: the trust was required to be irrevocable, perpetual and inalienable. Once property was declared waqf by its owner, the trust thereby created was irrevocable. It means (i) </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">inalienable lands used for charitable purposes</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> and (ii) pious endowments.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>. . . (14)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Mussalman Waqf Validating Act (VI of 1913)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 2(1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 105%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The origin of Waqf can be traced to the impulse of Muslims to do charitable deeds i.e. to endow property ‘in the way of the Almighty Allah’. According to Section 2(1) </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">of the Mussalman Waqf Validating Act, 1913</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> “Waqf” means the permanent dedication by a person professing the Mussalman faith of any property for any purpose recognized by the Musslman law as religious, pious or charitable.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span>. . . (15)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Bangol Waqf Act (XIII of 1934)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 6(10)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">According to section 6(10) of the Bangol </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Waqf Act, 1934 ‘Waqf’ means the permanent</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> dedication by a person professing Islam of any movable or immovable property for any purpose recognized by the Islamic Law as pious, religious or charitable and includes a waqf by user.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>. . . (15)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Waqfs Ordinance (I of 1962)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 2</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The waqf is irrevocable after possession is handed over to the Mutawlli. The waqif divests himself of the ownership of the property and of everything in the nature of contract from the moment the waqf is created. In purely metaphorical sense the expression “ownership of God” is used but unlike Hindu Law, since conception of a personal God is not recogniszed, there is no ownership of God or no property belongs to God in the Jural sense, although the ownership of the property becomes reverted in God because God is originally owner of all thing.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                          </span>. . . (16)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Bengol Waqf Act (XIII of 1934)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 70</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Waqf Commissioner and Mutawalli were not impleaded as parts in view of section 70 of the Bengol Waqf Act, 1934 any judgment and decree passed in respect of disputed waqf properly is not binding upon the Waqf Commissioner/ Administrator or Mutwalli of the waqf property. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>. . . (18) </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Waqf Ordinance (I of 1962)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 56</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Bengal Waqf Act (XIII of 1934)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 53</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The object, for which the property in question has been dedicated, is charitable, </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">pious or religious in nature and a portion of the</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> usufructs should be used by the descendents. Therefore, the dedication was complete and </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">it could not be divested for any other purposes.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Therefore, when a property can be used only </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">for religious or charitable purpose, it acquires</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> a permanent character. The waqf property </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">vests in the implied ownership of the Almighty</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">in the sense that nobody can claim ownership</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> of it. Even in waqf al aulad, the property is dedicated to the Almighty and only the usufructs are used by the descendents. Once the property is given to waqf, it remains for the waqf for ever. The property cannot be alienated or transferred nor is it subject to the rights of inheritance. It cannot be sold or given away to anybody except in accordance with law. The Islamic Law is a sacred Law, </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">and, thus transaction, or obligation is measured</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> by the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">standards of religious and moral rules. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Those</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;"> rules are developed through analogical</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">reasoning by Muslim Jurists. When ownership</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> of the waqf property is relinquished by the waqif, it cannot be acquired by any other person, rather it is arrested or detained. In </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">section 56 of the Bangladesh Waqfs Ordinance</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> 1962 Mutwalli’s power of alienation of waqf property has been restricted like section 53 of the Bengal Waqf Act, 1934 where the bar to transfer of immovable property of a waqf was provided.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>. . . (19)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Bengal Waqf Act (XIII of 1934)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 70(1)(4)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In every suit or proceeding in respect of any waqf property the court shall issue notice to the Commissioner at the cost of the party instituting such suit and proceeding and, in absence of such notice any decree or order passed in the suit or proceeding shall be declared void. <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>. . . (20)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Waqfs Ordinance (I of 1962) </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 2(12)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Waqf property and the same was not transferred by its actual owner, by the impugned deeds, title of the disputed waqf property had not been vested to the recipients of those deeds and those are mere papers transaction.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>. . .(22)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the Appellants:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> Mr. Syed Amirul Islam, Senior Advocate, instructed by Syed Mahbubar Rahman, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the Respondents:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> Mr. Farid Ahmed, Advocate instructed by Mr. Md. Taufique Hossain, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">Hasan Foez Siddique, J:</span></u></strong><u> </u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">This appeal is directed against the judgment and order dated 24.04.2008 passed by the High Court Division in Civil Revision No.1266 of 1999 making the Rule absolute reversing the judgment and decree dated 09.03.1999 passed by the then Subordinate Judge-in-charge, Patuakhali in Title Appeal No.14 of 1997 reversing those dated 03.02.1997 passed by the Senior Assistant Judge, Patuakhali Sadar, Patuakhali in Title Suit No.40 of 1993.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The relevant facts, for the disposal of this appeal, are that the appellant instituted the aforesaid suit for declaration that the sale deeds described in schedule ‘Ka’ to the plaint are collusive, void, fraudulent, inoperative and those are not binding upon the plaintiff stating, inter alia, that the plaintiff is the Mutwalli of Md. Asaq Waqf Estate. The land described in the schedule ‘Kha’ to the plaint is the waqf property of the said Waqf Estate and the same was enrolled vide E.C. No.10481. The plaintiff was appointed as Mutwalli of the said Estate on 08.09.1986. He filed an application under Section 64 of the Waqf Ordinance to the Waqf Administrator for eviction of the unauthorized occupants from ‘Kha’ scheduled land. The Waqf Administrator, by an order dated 04.01.1993, directed the plaintiff to file a suit in the Civil Court for declaration that the kabala deeds as described in the schedule-‘Ka’ to the plaint are void, inoperative and those are not binding upon the plaintiff. Accordingly, the plaintiff filed instant suit against respondents impugning the kabala deeds, (1)deed No.3360 dated 16.03.1976 executed by Md. Fazlul Karim Howlader in favour of Mozaffar Mridha; (2) deed No.1003 dated 20.04.1962 executed by Abdul Karim Mridha in favour of Abdul Gani and (3) deed No.11889 dated 07.10.1965 executed by Abdul Karim Mridha in favour of Ansaruddin Mollah in respect of the land as described in schedule-Kha to the plaint stating that those ‘Kha’ scheduled land are waqf property by virtue of waqf deed executed by Md. Asoq Ali and no one was entitled to transfer the same except taking the prior permission of waqf administrator and for the benefit of the waqf estate which was not taken before execution of those deeds.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The defendant-respondents contested the suit contending that the land measuring an area of 2.48 acres out of 3.03 acres appertaining to C.S. Khatian No.136 and Plot No.2275 and R.S. Khatian No.1 and Plot No.4203 was recorded in the name of Nirmal Kantha Roy who auction purchased the same on 24.03.1941. Md. Fazlul Karim and Abdul Karim took settlement of the said land from Nirmal Kantha Roy in 1348 B.S. They defaulted to pay rent of years 1351 to 1354 B.S. to the landlord. Thus, Nirmal Kantha filed Rent Suit No.398 of 1948 and got decree and, in execution of the said decree, the said land was again sold in auction. Hossain Ali and Keramat Ali auction purchased the same on 21.07.1948. Meanwhile, Fazlul Karim and Abdul Karim paid the auction money. Consequently, their raiyoti interest was not extinguished. They filed Title Suit No.488 of 1956 for permanent injunction against Hossain Ali and others and got decree. These defendants, purchasing the suit land by the impugned kabala deeds, have been possessing the same. The suit should be dismissed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The trial Court dismissed the suit. The plaintiff preferred appeal and the appellate Court allowed the appeal and decreed the suit. Then the defendants filed a civil revisional application in the High Court Division and obtained Rule. The High Court Division, by the impugned judgment and order, made the said Rule absolute. Thus, the plaintiff has preferred this appeal getting leave.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Syed Amirul Islam, learned Senior Counsel appearing for the appellant, submits that the High Court Division failed to consider that the alleged auction in 1941 was held without serving any notice to the Wakf Commissioner and Mutwalli of the waqf estate and that they were not impleaded in the Rent Suit as well inasmuch as they were the necessary parties. He submits that the High Court Division erred in law in interfering the decision of the appellate Court inasmuch as it was the duty of Fazlul Karim, father of the plaintiff Mutwalli, to pay rent and taxes of the waqf property from the income of the said property. He concocted the story of selling the waqf property in auction for non-payment of rent. He could not claim waqf property as his personal property. He submits that the High Court Division failed to notice that Fazlul Karim continued to be Mutwalli of Md. Asaq Estate after its enrollment vide E.C. No.10481 on 30.01.1942 in the office of Waqf Commissioner he could not become owner of the waqf property and as a manager of the same it was his duty to protect the waqf property. He submits that pursuant to rent decree passed in Rent Suit No.398 of 1948 the property could not be said to have lost its waqf character.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Farid Ahmed, learned Senior Counsel appearing for the respondents, submits that the property in question was sold in auction in 1941 and auction purchaser settled the same to Fazlul Karim and Abdul Karim. Thereafter, the landlord filed Rent Suit No.398 of 1948 and got decree and the same was again sold in auction in execution of the said decree and one Hossain Ali and Keramat Ali auction purchased the same but Fazlul Karim and Abdul Karim, the judgment debtors, paid the entire auction money and protected their ownership in the property and that the defendants are the subsequent purchasers from Fazlul Karim and Abdul Karim, the High Court Division, considering all those facts and evidence on record, rightly made the said Rule absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The High Court Division observed that the property, in question, was made waqf by virtue of the waqf deed dated 30.01.1922. The High Court Division held that the same lost its waqf character due to the auction held in 1941 and finally it observed that, at present, the suit land is not the property of said Asaq Waqf Estate. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">It is the case of the plaintiff that suit land originally belonged to Mohammad Asoq. From the judgment of Title Suit No. </span><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";mso-bidi-font-weight:bold'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(488 of 1956,208 of 1958) </span><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";mso-bidi-font-weight:bold'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span><![endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>(ext-Ga) it appears that the plaintiffs of that suit, namely, Mahammad Fazlul Karim Howlader and Abdul Karim Howlader sons of Haji Mohammad Asoq admitted that their father Asoq Ali Fakir, was Usat Nim Howla raiyat and his name was duly recorded in Khatian No.136. The High Court Division observed that admittedly, by virtue of registered waqf deed dated 30.01.1922 (ext.3), the suit land became the property of Md. Asoq Waqf Estate. In such view of the matter, we have no hesitation to hold that the suit land originally belonged to Mohammad Asoq. From ext.3 it appears that Mohammad Asoq executed a waqf deed in respect of the suit land and his other lands. From waqf deed, it further appears that Asoq had 4 sons namely Mohammad Hachon, Mohammad Hossain, Mohammad Fazlul Karim andm Mohammad Abdul Karim. Mohammad Asoq appointed himself as first Mutwalli of the waqf Estate and it was stipulated that after his death, his first son Mohammad Hashon would be the Mutwalli. In the waqf deed it was, inter alia, stated, “</span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Avwg RxweZ _vKv ch©šÍ Avwg GB IqvKd †_‡K †gvZIqvj¬x _vwKqv wbg¥wjwLZ wbqvgvwa‡b Kvh©¨ Kwie| Avgvi AeZ©gv‡b GB IqvKdbvgvi wbqg Abymv‡i Avgvi †Rô¨cyÎ MªnxZv k«x Lvb gnv¤§` nvPb †gvZqvj¬x _vwKqv wb‡g¥i ZcwQ‡ji wjwLZ m¤úwË mvb I msi¶b Kwi‡eb| †gvËvKxb †gvZqvj¬x wbhy³ nB‡j IqvK‡di dvÛ nB‡Z Zvnvi wb‡Ri fib ‡cvl‡bi e¨q BZ¨vw` jwn‡eb bv| Avgvi wbhy³ ev †gvZIqvj¬x Af¨šÍ‡i Avgvi Kwbô 3 cyÎ ga¨ whwb mr we‡ePK I eyw×gvb Ges m¤úwË i¶v Kivi Dchy³ nB‡eb wZwbB †gvZIqvj¬x _vwK‡eb| GBiæc cyÎ‡cŠÎvw` μ‡g whwb mr we‡ePK I eyw×gvb Ges Kvh©¶g nb wZwb †gvZIqvj¬x nB‡e| †gvZIqvj¬x IqvK‡di †óU nB‡Z Avcb fib †cvl‡bi e¨vq BZ¨vw` cvB‡eb bv| †gvZIqvj¬xMY m¤úwË m¤^Üxq kvmb msi¶b I gwjKv‡bi cªvc¨ ivR¯e BZ¨vw` Av`vq Rb¨ wb‡g¥i Zckxj wjwLZ 21bs m¤úwËi 2275/ `v‡Mi| /. `yB Kvwb bvj Rwg hvnv Avgvi wbR Lvm `L‡j Av‡Q Zvnv †gvZIqvj¬x Avcb Lvm `L‡j ivwLqv Z`Dc¯^Z¡ Øvivq AÎ IqvK‡di wjwLZ m¤úwËi ivR¯e BZ¨vw` cwi‡kva Kwi‡eb Z` Ab¨_vq †gvZIqvj¬x c` nB‡Z Aemi nB‡eb Ges Zr ev‡` Avgvi eswkq Zckxj D³ †gvZIqvj¬x c‡` wbhy³ nB‡eb| IqvK†di m¤úwË m¤^‡Ü hLb †h †`Iqvbx wK ‡dŠR`vix †h †Kvb cªKv‡ii †hiæc †Kvb †gvKÏgv Dcw¯’Z nq Zvnv †gvZIqvj¬x wbe©vn Kwi‡eb Ges Zvnvi Dchy³ LiP IqvK‡di †óU enb Kwi‡eb| †ó‡Ui UvKv †_‡K Rgv †Kvb wb®úwË wK Kvh©¨ Kwi‡Z nB‡j †gvZIqvj¬x wb‡Ri Awfcªvq Ges eskxq Ab¨vb¨ e¨vw³Mb mwnZ civgk© g‡Z hvnv fvj nq we‡ePbv K‡i ev ‡mB cªKv‡iB Kwi‡Z cvwi‡eb| †gvZIqvj¬x †ó‡Ui nvwb RbK ‡Kvb Kvh©¨ Kwi‡j I Zvnv mve¨¯’¨ nB‡j D³ †gvZIqvj¬x Kvh¨© nB‡Z Zvnv‡K Aemi Kwiqv Avgvi Mªvg¯n f`ª wewkó e¨w³MY Ab¨ Avgvi eskxq _v‡K †gvZIqvj¬x g‡bvbxZ _vwK‡eb| wZwbB †gvZIqvj¬x nB‡eb †gvZIqvj¬x wbhy³ Mªvg¯n f`ª wewkó e¨w³M‡Yi ci m¤ú~Y© ¶gZv iB‡jb|</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The waqif Mohammad Asoq started the recitation his waqf deed saying <strong>“</strong></span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">---------†Lv`vZvjvi K…cvq Avwg mvgxË¡ mg~‡ni AwaKvi nBqvwQ| †mB †Lv`vZvjvi bv‡g mr Kv‡h©v D‡Ï‡k¨ Avgvi ¯^‡Ë¦i Zckxj ewY©Z m¤úwË n‡Z Avgvi ¯^Áv‡b my¯n kix‡i mijvšÍ-------- IqvKd Kwijvg|Ó</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">It is the case of the contesting defendants that one Nirmal Kantha Roy auction purchased the land of C.S. Khatian No. 136 (disputed Khatian) on 24.03.1941 in a Revenue sale. From whom, Fazlul Karim and Abdul Karim (two sons of Waqif Mohammad Asoq) took settlement of the said land. The High Court Division did not find any paper to prove the facts of Revenue Sale and auction purchase by Nirmal Kantha Roy. We also did not find any documentary evidence in support of the claim of Revenue sale and auction. The High Court Division observed that in the plaint the plaintiff admitted the existence of that auction and purchase of the same by Nirmal Kantha Roy. We have perused the contents of the plaint of this suit. We do not find any such admission of the plaintiff in the plaint that Nirmal Kantha Roy auction purchasedthe suit land in Revenue Sale held on 24.03.1941. The High Court Division misread the plaint, thereby, erroneously observed so. The defendants also did not produce any papers regarding settlement alleged to have been given by Nirmal Kantha to Fazlul Karim and Abdul Karim, the executants of the impugned deeds.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">From ext. ‘Ka’ it appears that Nirmal Kantha Roy filed Rent Suit No.398 of 1948 on 15.04.1948 against Fazlul Karim and one Abdul Mridha stating that he purchased touzi No.1565 of Taluk Nabkeshore Datta in Rent sale under the provision of Act II of 1859 on 24.03.1941 and got sale certificate and took over possession through Court. In that suit, he prayed for realization of defaulted rent of Rs.1104/-. From ext ‘Ka-1’ copy of the decree dated 24.08.1948 it appears that the defendants deposited the decreetal dues with cost. Copy of the judgment of the said suit has not been filed. From ext-‘Kha’ certified copy of the register of application for the execution of the decree it appears that auction held in Rent Suit No.398 of 1948 was set aside and the Execution case was disposed of on full satisfaction on 01.03.1949. In the said suit, neither wakf Commissioner nor the Mutwalli of Asoq Ali Waqf Estate was impleaded as party. From the judgment and decree passed in Title Suit No. </span><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";mso-bidi-font-weight:bold'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(488 of 1956,208 of 1958) </span><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";mso-bidi-font-weight:bold'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span><![endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>(ext.Ga and Ga-1) it appears that Mohammad Fazlul Karim Howlader and Abdul Karim Howlader sons of late Mohammad Asoq, filing the said suit, obtained decree against Hoshen Ali Fakir son of Sabbat Ali Fakir and Keramat Ali Fakir son of Monsur Ali Fakir. They are nobody of the Waqf Estate. In that case also neither the Wakf Commissioner nor the Mutwalli of Asoq waqf Estate was impleaded as party. It is to be mentioned here again that in the waqf deed the waqif categorically stated that “</span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">IqvK‡di m¤úwË m¤^‡Ü hLb †h †`Iqvbx wK †dŠR`vix †h †Kvb cªKv‡ii †hiæc †Kvb<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>†gvKÏgv Dcw¯nZ nq Zvnv †gvZIqvj¬x wbe©vn Kwi‡eb|</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">” It was the duty of Fazlul Karim and Abdul Karim to pay the defaulted rent or decreetal dues to protect the waqf property which was made by their father. Without doing so, they executed the impugned deeds. Since in all those transactions and suits Waqf Commissioner and <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Mutwalli of the Waqf Estate were not impleaded</span> as party those are not binding upon them.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The origin of waqf is to the direct prescriptious, of the Prophet (Sm)Ibn Omer as stated in the Jamaa ut Tirmizi that “Omer (R:) had acquired a piece of land in (the canton of) Khaibar, and proceeded to the Prophet (Sm) and sought his counsel, to make the most pious use of it, (whereupon) the Prophet (Sm) declared, ‘tie up’ the property (asl or corpus) and devote the usufruct to human beings, and it is not to be sold or made the subject of gift or inheritance; devote its produce to your children, your kindred, and the poor in the way of God. In accordance with this rule Omer dedicated the property, in question, and the waqf contained in existence for several centuries until the land became wastage. (relied on Commentaries on Mohommedan Law by Amir Ali Syed).</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">According to Imam Abu Hanifa the meaning of waqf is the detention of a specific thing in the ownership of waqf and the devoting of its profit or products “in charity of poors or other good objects”. Imam Abu Yusuf said, “Waqf signifies the extinction of the waqif’s ownership in the thing dedicated and detention of all the thing in the implied ownership of the Almighty Allah, in such a manner that its profits may revert to or be applied ‘for the benefit of Mankind.’ </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Three basic principles governed the waqf: the trust was required to be irrevocable, perpetual, and inalienable. Once property was declared waqf by its owner, the trust thereby created was irrevocable. It means (i) inalienable lands used for charitable purposes and (ii) pious endowments. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The origin of Waqf can be traced to the impulse of Muslims to do charitable deeds i.e., to endow property ‘in the way of the Almighty Allah’. According to Section 2(1) of the Mussalman Waqf Validating Act, 1913 “Waqf” means the permanent dedication by a person professing the Mussalman faith of any property for any purpose recognized by the Musslman law as religious, pious or charitable. According to section 6(10) of the Bangol Waqf Act, 1934 ‘waqf’ means the permanent dedication by a person professing Islam of any movable or <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">immovable property for any purpose recognized</span> by the Islamic Law as pious, religious or charitable and includes a waqf by user. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The waqf is irrevocable after possession is handed over to the Mutawalli. The waqif divests himself of the ownership of the property and of everything in the nature of contract from the moment the waqf is created. In purely metaphorical sense the expression “ownership of God” is used but unlike Hindu Law, since conception of a personal God is not recognized, there is no ownership of God or no property belongs to God in the Jural sense, although the ownership of the property becomes reverted in God because God is originally owner of all thing. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">We have already found that the High Court Division held that the disputed property is waqf property of Mohammad Asoq Waqf Estate created by a registered waqf deed executed and registered on 30.01.1922 (ext.3) which was duly enrolled in the office of Waqf Commissioner vide E.C. No.10481 on 30.01.1942 under the provision of the Bengol Waqf Act, 1934. Section 70 of the Bengol Waqf Act 1934 specifically provides:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Section 70(1): In every suit or proceeding in respect of any wakf property or of a mutwalli as such except a suit or proceeding for the recovery of rent by or on behalf of the mutwalli the Court shall issue notice to the Commissioner at the cost of the <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">party instituting such suit or proceeding.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(2) Before any wakf property is notified for sale in execution of a decree, notice shall be given by the Court to the Commissioner. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(3) Before any wakf property is notified for sale for the recovery of any revenue, case, rates or taxes due to the Crown or to local authority notice shall be given to the whose order the sale is notified. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(4) In the absence of a notice under sub-section (1) any decree or order passed in the suit or proceeding shall be declared void, if the Commissioner, within one month of is coming to know of such suit or proceeding, applied to the Court in this behalf. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(5) In the absence of a notice under subsection (2) or sub-section (3) the sale shall be declared void, if the Commissioner, within one month of his coming to know of the sale, applies in this behalf to the Court, or other authority under whose order the sale was held.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Since Waqf Commissioner and Mutawalli were not impleaded as parts in view of section 70 of the Bengol Waqf Act, 1934 any judgment and decree passed in respect of disputed waqf properly is not binding upon the Waqf Commissioner/Administrator or Mutwalli of the waqf property. We do not find anything in the pleading in the contesting defendants or in the evidence that the provisions of section 70 of the Bengol Waqf Act, 1934 had been complied with in the proceeding of alleged Rent Sale, Rent Suit No.389 of 1948 and in Title Suit No.488 of 1956. We have already found that no evidence was produced in support of the claim of the defendant that Nirmal Kantha auction purchased the suit land in Rent Sale allegedly held on 24.03.1941.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">From the recital of waqf deed it appears that the object, for which the property in question has been dedicated, is charitable, pious or religious in nature and a portion of the usufructs should be used by the descendents. Therefore, the dedication was complete and it could not be divested for any other purposes. Therefore, when a property can be used only for religious or charitable purpose, it acquires a permanent character. The waqf property vests in the implied ownership of the Almighty inthe sense that nobody can claim ownership of it. Even in waqf al aulad, the property is dedicated to the Almighty and only the usufructs are used by the descendents. Once the property is given to waqf, it remains for the waqf for ever. The property cannot be alienated or transferred nor is it subject to the rights of inheritance. It cannot be sold or given away to anybody except in accordance with law. The Islamic Law is a sacred Law, and, thus transaction, or obligation is measured by the standards of religious and moral rules. Those rules are developed through analogical reasoning by Muslim Jurists. When ownership of the waqf property is relinquished by the waqif, it cannot be acquired by any other person, rather it is arrested or detained. In section 56 of the Bangladesh Waqfs Ordinance 1962 Mutwalli’s power of alienation of waqf property has been restricted like section 53 of the Bengal Waqf Act, 1934 where the bar to transfer of immovable property of a waqf was provided.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">From plain reading of section 70(1)(4) of the Bengal Waqf Act, 1934 it is apparent that in </span><span style="font-size: 11pt;">every suit or proceeding in respect of any waqf property the court shall issue notice to the Commissioner at the cost of the party instituting such suit and proceeding and, in absence of such notice any decree or order passed in the suit or proceeding shall be declared void.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">21.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">       </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">We have already found that no such notice was issued of alleged Rent Sale, Rent Suit No.398 of 1948 and Title Suit No. 488 of 1956 upon Waqf Commissioner and Mutwalli. Even they were not impleaded as party in those suit or proceeding. In such view of the matter, the decree or order passed in those suits or proceedings are not binding upon the Waqf Commissioner and by those decrees or orders the Waqf character of that suit land had not been extinguished.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">22.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Since the property, in question, is waqf property and the same was not transferred by its actual owner, by the impugned deeds, title of the disputed waqf property had not been vested to the recipients of those deeds and those are mere papers transaction.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">23.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Accordingly, we find substance in the appeal. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">24.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Thus, the appeal is allowed. Impugned judgment and order of the High Court Division is set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 95%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue__AUGUST_%2018(2)__C.%20A.552%20of%2009__Hasan%20Foez%20Siddique,%20J._AD__4_.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 95%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: BatangChe; font-variant: small-caps; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Civil Appeal No. </span></u></strong></a><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 95%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: BatangChe; font-variant: small-caps; mso-ansi-language: EN;">552 of 2009</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(From the judgment and order dated 24.04.2008 passed by the High Court Division in Civil Revision No. 1266 of 1999.)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
657	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Kabir Sikder Vs. The State and another, (Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarker , J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 23406 of 2017  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Rezaul Haque, J And Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Md. Kamrul Ahasan, Advocate,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Kabir Sikder </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  The State and another  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Criminal Procedure </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-01</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; font-variant: small-caps; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(criminal miscellaneous jurisdiction)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto;"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 106.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top" width="141"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Md. Rezaul Haque, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">And</strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Muhammad Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J</strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">12.04.2018</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 15.6pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="21"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue%20__AUGUST_18(2)__Crl.%20Misc.%2023406%20of%2017__Muhammad%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarkar,%20J.__3.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Md. Kabir Sikder</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: right;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . Accused Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The State and another </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .Opposite-Parties</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: left;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Code of Crim</span></strong></span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="color: #000000;">inal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 200</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">If the claimed dealings between the complainant and the accused emerge to be equivocal or cryptic or obscure from the petition of complaint and the statements of the complainant made under Section 200 </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">CrPC together with the documents produced</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> before the Magistrate, it would not be possible for the Magistrate to make any primary assessment as to whether the offence of cheating or breach of trust has been committed for the purpose of taking cognizance of the said offence/s. The Magistrate, however, can take cognizance of the offence, upon ignoring the averments of the petition of complaint, if the Magistrate at the time of examining the complainant under Section 200 of the CrPC in tandem </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">with carrying out scrutiny of the documentary</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> evidence, if any, finds the complainant’s allegation to be putatively plausible.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span>. . . (9)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Sections 200 and 202</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">When the Magistrate decides to take cognizance of the alleged offence/s, s/he is duty bound to examine the complainant on oath and reduce the substance of the examination in writing. When the complaint is made in writing and its contents appear to the Magistrate to be ambiguous, the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Magistrate either should ask the complainant</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> to come up with a fresh application clearly disclosing the offence or, in the alternative, pass an order for carrying out an inquiry under Section 202 CrPC and, after looking at the fresh petition of complaint or inquiry report, as the case may be, the Magistrate then would be in a better position to decide whether to proceed for taking cognizance. Non-compliance of the above practice, however, would not vitiate the proceedings. The purpose of observance of the above path is to gain <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">prima facie</em> satisfaction by the Magistrate as to commission of offence, for, the Magistrate is required to be satisfied either from the petition of complaint or from the statements of the complainant made under Section 200 CrPC or from the inquiry report, as the case may be, that any one of it discloses commission of offence. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Despite existence of any inconsistency between</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> the version of the petition of complaint and </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the statements of the complainant made under</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> Section 200 CrPC, when the Magistrate takes cognizance, the presumption is that </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">the concerned Magistrate has been primarily</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> satisfied about commission of offence. ...(17)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 561 A</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In an appropriate and fit case, order of framing charge may be quashed if it appears to the High Court Division that the trial Court failed to notice that the prosecution materials are not sufficient to prosecute the accused or it was not brought to the notice of the trial Court that provision of any particular law does not permit to prosecute the accused.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                        </span>. . .(20)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 227</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Penal Code (XLV of 1860)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Sections 406, 417 and 506</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">The trial Court is empowered to alter charge</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> at any stage before pronouncement of the Judgment, the charges of breach of trust and criminal intimidation may eventually be dropped by the trial Court following taking deposition of the witnesses, if the said allegations are not corroborated by the evidence. Depending on the weight of the evidence adduced at the trial, while the complainant would have the expectation to prove his case, it might come out to be its reverse as well.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">               </span>. . . (20)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Code of Criminal Procedure (V of 1898)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 561A </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">The allegation is of civil nature debarring filing of a criminal case.
