line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">27.11.2017</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 51.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue__AUGUST_%2018(2)__C.%20P.%201894%20of%2016__Mirza%20Hussain%20Haider,%20J._AD__1__with%20july%20LAST.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 301.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mohammad Shafi Ullah, Director (Retd), Directorate of Relief and Rehabilitation, 92-93, Mohakhali, Dhaka-1212- At present- House No. 29/C(4<sup>th</sup> Floor), Asad Avenue, Mohammadpur, Dhaka.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">             </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Petitioner</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-Versus</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Government of Bangladesh, represented by the Secretary, Ministry of Disaster Management and Relief, Bangladesh Secretariat, Dhaka and others.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Respondents</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p style="text-align: left;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Words and Phrases</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Equality before law. </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">The term ‘Equality before law’ should not be interpreted in its absolute sense to hold that all persons are equal in all respect disregarding different conditions and circumstances in which they are placed or with special quality and characteristics which some of them may possess, but which are lacking in others. In fact the term ‘equality before law’ means all persons are not equal in all respects but the persons similarly situated should be treated alike. Equal protection of law is a guarantee, that similar people should be dealt with in a similar way/manner and that people placed on different circumstances cannot be treated uniformly to all persons disregarding the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">basic differences among them. If these differences </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">are identified, then the persons may be classified into different groups or categories according to those distinctions. . . . (14)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Administrative Tribunals Act (VII of 1981)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 4(2)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">‘Promotion is not a matter of right’. It is to be earned by meritorious service along with efficiency and good conduct, character and integrity. Seniority, though not the sole criteria for promotion but it is one of the primary requirements for promotion.</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Seniority alone does not create right to promotion. Along with it some other factors, like merit, sincerity, honesty, integrity, efficiency, sense of responsibilities and values etc. are also to be taken into consideration for promotion.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Keeping such factors in mind, it is for the authority to make decision as regards the matter of promotion of an employee concerned. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The petitioner being not in service and having not raised any such question any time during his tenure in the service, before his retirement, he cannot, under any circumstances, equate himself with respondents No. 5 and 6 and as such he cannot claim promotion and benefit after two and half years of his retirement on receipt of the full pension benefits without any objection on the basis of equating him with the said two respondents. His case can never be considered to be at per or of equal status with respondents No. 5 and 6. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">The petitioner is not at per or is not in a similarly placed position/category. Nor he can be termed as equal amongst the equals. Thus he cannot claim that he has been discriminated and thereby he has been deprived of getting the same benefit or treatment as has been given to respondents No. 5 and 6. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span></span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: right; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . . (13, 15, 16 and 18)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For the Petitioner:</span></strong> <span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mrs.Sufia Khatun, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For the Respondents:</span></strong> <span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.1pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Not represented. </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; font-variant: small-caps; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mirza Hussain Haider, J</span></u></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">This civil petition for leave to appeal is directed against the order dated 04.04.2016, passed by the Administrative Appellate Tribunal, Dhaka, in Administrative Appellate Tribunal Appeal No. 256 of 2013, allowing the appeal and thereby setting aside the order dated 26.09.2013, passed by the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Administrative Tribunal-2 Dhaka, in A.T Case No. 61 of 2012(Original A.T. Case No. 53 of 2010) allowing the case and thereby directing the authority<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>to give promotion to the petitioner with retrospective effect<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>from 25.09.1988 in the post of Deputy Director and thereafter in the post of Director from 25.09.1992 along with all back salaries and allowances in respect of those posts and other attending benefits.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Facts leading to filing of this civil Petition for Leave to Appeal, in brief, are:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>The present petitioner filed A.T. Case No. 53 of 2010 under section 4(2) of the Administrative Tribunals Act, 1980 before the Administrative Tribunal-1, Dhaka, stating, inter alia, that he is a freedom fighter and successfully attended the Special Superior Service Examination under the Public Service Commission in 1972. As per merit list, pursuant to the said examination, he was supposed to be appointed as Class-I Gazetted Officer but inadvertently he was appointed in the post of Sub-Divisional Relief and Rehabilitation Officer on 25.3.1974 under the present respondents No. 1 to 4 vide Memo No. GENL-2/74/658(45) which was a Class-II Gazetted Officer post. On bringing the matter to the notice of the concerned authority, the said post of Sub-Divisional Relief and Rehabilitation Officer was upgraded as Class-I Gazetted Officer with effect from 09.01.1983. Thereafter the petitioner was promoted to the post of District Relief and Rehabilitation Officer on 05.09.1983 where he joined on 09.10.1983. Being<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>promoted to the post of Deputy Director on 28.06.1998 the petitioner joined the said post on 01.07.1998 and lastly being promoted to the post of Director on 08.03.2006 he joined the said post on the same day. After completion of his service the petitioner went on retirement on 25.01.2008. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 109%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">On the other hand, respondents No. 5 and 6 herein joined Jatiya Jubo Sangstha (National Youth Organization) in 1981 as Sub-Divisional Executive Officers. However, they lost their jobs after abolition of the said department on 21.4.1982 and subsequently with the approval of the Ministry of Establishment the said two respondents got fresh appointment and were absorbed in the Relief and Rehabilitation Department, as Assistant Directors where they joined on 30.01.1989 and 07.02.1989 respectively and thereafter both of them were promoted to the post of Deputy Director on 05.01.2004 and 11.12.2007 respectively. As per Recruitment Rules, 1995, although the said respondents No. 5 and 6 had requisite qualifications and became eligible for promotion to the post of Director but the authority did not take any step in that respect. Hence they filed AT Cases No. 48 of 2006 and 49 of 2006 before the Administrative Tribunal for getting promotion with retrospective effect. Having succeeded in the said cases the authority gave them promotion with retrospective effect in compliance with the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>order passed in the aforesaid cases.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">On 27.10.2010, upon coming to know about the said matter, the petitioner filed a petition before the concerned authority for reconsideration of his case by review stating, inter alia, that since his service record was very clean, unblemished and no adverse remark being made there in his ACR and since, as per Service Rules, 1995, he is entitled to get promotion to the post of Deputy Director and Director with retrospective effect from 25.3. 1987 and 25.3.1992 respectively along with financial benefits and all attending benefits and since the respondents No. 5 and 6 have been given such promotion and benefits, he be given the same. But the authority did not do anything on the said review petition<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>even within two months from the date of filing of the same. Hence the petitioner filed the aforesaid AT Case No. 53 of 2010 before the Administrative Tribunal-1, Dhaka, which has been renumbered as AT Case No. 61 of 2012 on transfer to the Administrative Tribunal-2 Dhaka.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The respondents contested the said case by filing<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>written statement denying the claims and material allegations made by the petitioner and contending, inter alia, that the petitioner was duly promoted to the higher posts<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and ultimately on completion of his service he retired on 25.1.2008 upon receiving all pension benefits without raising any objection, whatsoever. It is further alleged that during his service period or at the time of promotion or even at the time of taking pension benefits the petitioner did not raise any such claim of promotion with retrospective effect nor did he lodge any complaint that he was not given promotion in due course. It is further contended that the petitioner claimed benefit of the order passed in AT Case No. 48 of 2006 and 49 of 2006 obtained by respondents No. 5 and 6 respectively, which he can not claim as he was neither<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>a party in the said cases nor any direction was given<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>in the said cases to deal with cases of similar nature or particularly in his favour. Hence the petitioner’s case is liable to be dismissed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The Tribunal upon hearing the parties and considering the materials on record allowed the petitioner’s A.T. case by the order <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">dated 26.09.2013, against which the government</span> preferred A.A.T. Appeal No. 256 of 2013 before the Administrative Appellate Tribunal, Dhaka, which has been allowed upon hearing the parties and on consideration of the materials on record by the order dated 04.04.2016 upon setting aside the order of the Tribunal dated 26.9.2013. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Being aggrieved by the aforesaid order dated 04.04.2016, the petitioner herein, filed the present civil petition for leave to appeal before this Division.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Mrs. Sufia Khatun, the learned Advocate-On-Record, appearing on behalf of the leave-petitioner submits that the Administrative Appellate Tribunal erred in law in not appreciating the fact that the petitioner was not only senior to respondents No. 5 and 6, but he also possessed other qualities like efficiency, good conduct, character, integrity, dynamic personality which are essential for consideration in case of promotion<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and his service record was all along clean, unblemished with no adverse remarks in the ACR and even no explanation, whatsoever, was ever called from him by the authority while discharging his duties and functions in his whole service career. Upon considering all these qualifications the Administrative Tribunal gave relief to the petitioner which the Appellate Tribunal failed to consider. She submits that the Appellate Tribunal failed to appreciate that pursuant to the order of the Tribunal respondent No.1 gave ante dated seniority and promotion to respondents No. 5 and 6 without preferring any appeal against the said order of the Administrative Tribunal<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>but in the case of the petitioner, instead of treating him equally along with respondents No. 5 and 6, the respondents treated him with mala fide, arbitrary and discriminatory manner and thereby refused to grant him promotion which the Tribunal upon considering all the materials on record granted in his favour.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>She also submits that by the order dated 4.10.2009 respondent No.1 having given ante-dated seniority and promotion to<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>respondents No. 5 and 6 but refused to do so in respect of the petitioner ignoring his review petition which is violative of the doctrine of equality, fairness and reasonableness as guaranteed under Articles 27, 29 and 31 of the Constitution of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Hence the order complained of herein is liable to be set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">No one represented the respondents.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Considering the facts and circumstances and the submissions as stated above, it appears that on 04.04.2010 the petitioner filed Administrative Tribunal Case No. 61 of 2012 (originally AT Case No. 53 of 2010) alleging that respondents No. 5 and 6, who were appointed in 1989, much later than the petitioner as Assistant Directors in the same department and were promoted as Deputy Directors on 05.01.2004 and 11.12.2007 respectively were given ante dated seniority and promotion with retrospective effect from the date of attaining their requisite length of service pursuant to the Tribunal’s order. But though the petitioner attained the requisite length of service and seniority for being promoted to the post of Director much earlier than those of the said two respondents, his case was not considered by the authority. Hence the petitioner also obtained similar order from the Tribunal, upon coming to know about the favour in respect of the respondents No. 5 and 6, after more than two and half years of his retirement but his case has not been considered. Thus the petitioner claimed that the authority instead of dealing with him equally, challenged the Tribunal’s order obtained by him, in appeal before the Appellate Tribunal in violation of and upon infringing his fundamental rights, which they did not do in the case of respondents No. 5 and 6.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Now the question is whether the petitioner,</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> under such circumstances, is entitled to get promotion and benefits with retrospective effect after he has gone on retirement with entire benefit and whether the authority failed to equate him with respondents No. 5 and 6 in dealing with his case and thereby he has been discriminated. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The Administrative Appellate Tribunal considering the materials on record and the law and also considering several decisions of the apex court, came to the conclusion that the petitioner is not eligible to get such promotion and benefit with retrospective effect nor can he be equated with respondents No. 5 and 6 and as such no question of discrimination arises in his case.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">By now it has already been settled that ‘promotion is not a matter of right’. It is to be earned by meritorious service along with efficiency and good conduct, character and integrity. Seniority, though not the sole criteria for promotion but it is one of the primary requirements for promotion. However, it appears from the submissions of the learned Advocate-on-Record for the petitioner that the petitioner claims retrospectivity of his promotion and benefits on the ground of seniority as well as equality.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The term ‘equality before law’ should not be interpreted in its absolute sense to hold that all persons are equal in all respect disregarding different conditions and circumstances in which they are placed or with special quality and characteristics which some of them may possess, but which are lacking in others. In fact the term ‘equality before law’ means all persons are not equal in all respects but the persons similarly situated should be treated alike. Equal protection of law is a guarantee, that similar people should be dealt with in a similar way/manner and that people placed on different circumstances cannot be treated uniformly to all persons disregarding the basic differences among them. If these differences are identified, then the persons may be classified into different groups or categories according to those distinctions.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The accepted principle is that seniority alone does not create right to promotion.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Along with it some other factors, like merit, sincerity, honesty, integrity, efficiency, sense of responsibilities and values etc. are also to be taken into consideration for promotion.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Keeping such factors in mind, it is for the authority to<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>make decision as regards the matter of promotion of an employee concerned. For the aforesaid reasons it would not be within the jurisdiction of the Court to direct an authority to promote a particular employee and thereby deprive the authority of considering the case of promotion of a<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>particular or any other employee in the background of the facts available to it. It is within the domain of the authority to make decision in the matter of promotion to its employee in the back ground of the facts available as well as upon due compliance with the rules/regulations, if any. If the decision so made is challenged then only it would be quite within the jurisdiction of the court to examine whether in arriving at such decision the authority has complied with the aforementioned requirements as well as the existing rules/regulations or that the authority proceeded on flawed procedure and material or left out materials which was very much integral to the matter of promotion process.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In the instant case the distinction, which can be drawn between the petitioner and respondents No. 5 and 6 is that the petitioner has gone on retirement upon accepting all retirement benefits without any objection whatsoever, whereas respondents No. 5 and 6 have not i.e. they were very much in service. Thus after two and half years of his retirement and upon receiving all retirement benefits,<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the petitioner cannot claim that he is equal with respondent No. 5 and 6, who are very much in service at the relevant time. From the materials on record, as well as from the facts and circumstances of the case as stated above, it is clear that the petitioner took a chance of comparing himself with respondents No. 5 and 6 and as they have been given promotion with retrospective effect he should also be given the same, treating him at per with them and as such he should not have been deprived, as he has been, according to him, being of equal status. But the case is quite different. The petitioner being not in service and having not raised any such question any time during his tenure in the service, before his retirement, he cannot, under any circumstances, equate himself with respondents No. 5 and 6 and as such he cannot claim promotion and benefit after two and half years of his retirement on receipt of the full pension benefits without any objection on the basis of equating him with the said two respondents. His case can never be considered to be at per or of equal status with respondents No. 5 and 6.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">On the other hand if it is taken into consideration that the petitioner made a prayer for review or made a representation for re-consideration of his case on the face of promotion of respondents No. 5 and 6 the same also cannot improve the petitioner’s case. Had it been a case that he had been trying hard to get such benefit prior to his retirement then the case probably would have been otherwise. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">So the question whether the petitioner, who is not in service, as against those of the respondents No. 5 and 6 who are in service, can claim that he has not been treated equally. The answer is emphatically no. Because the petitioner is not at per or is not in a similarly placed position/category. Nor he can be termed as equal amongst the equals. Thus he cannot claim that he has been discriminated and thereby he has been deprived of getting the same benefit or treatment as has been given to respondents No. 5 and 6.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 26.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Considering the facts and circumstances as stated hereinabove, and having gone through the impugned order of the Administrative Appellate Tribunal we are of the view that the Administrative Appellate Tribunal correctly appreciated the law and considered the facts of the case and came to a correct conclusion for which it is difficult to find any legal infirmity/flaw in the same and as such there is nothing to interfere with. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 115%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 26.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Accordingly, this civil petition for leave to appeal is dismissed without any order as to cost.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Ed.</span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 90%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue__AUGUST_%2018(2)__C.%20P.%201894%20of%2016__Mirza%20Hussain%20Haider,%20J._AD__1__with%20july%20LAST.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 90%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Comic Sans MS'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL NO.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>1894 OF 2016</span></u></strong></a><u></u></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 90%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 90%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(<span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">From the judgment and order dated 04.04.2016, passed </span></span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 9.0pt; line-height: 90%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">by the Administrative Appellate Tribunal in Administrative</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 90%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> Appellate Tribunal Appeal No. 256 of 2013). </span></p></div></div></div></div>
660	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Moulavi Abdul Wahab Vs. Nur Ahmed and others, (Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL NO.  1260 OF 2011  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J,  Nazmun Ara Sultana, J Muhammad Imman Ali, J, Md. Nizamul Huq, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. A.J Mohammad Ali, Senior Advocate instructed by Mr. Md. Taufique Hossain, Advocate-on-Record.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ (AD)     </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2016</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Moulavi Abdul Wahab </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Nur Ahmed and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Supreme Court (High Court Division) Rules </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-01</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CIVIL)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; height: 204px; width: 629px; margin-right: auto;" width="655"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes; height: 112.85pt;"><td style="width: 255.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J, </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Nazmun Ara Sultana, J</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Muhammad Imman Ali, J,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Md. Nizamul Huq, J</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">31.03.2016</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 42.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue__AUGUST_%2018(2)__C.%20P.%201260%20of%2011__Md.%20Abdul%20Wahhab%20Miah__AD__3.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 287.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Moulavi Abdul Wahab</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Appellant </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-Versus</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Nur Ahmed and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Respondents</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold', serif; letter-spacing: -0.6pt;">Supreme Court (High Court Division) Rules, 1973</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;">Chapter VIA (3) (4)</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">It struck our conscience how a learned Judge after recalling the order making a matter out of list hear the same on that the very date and dispose the same, in the absence of the petitioner.</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">We deprecate this kind of exercise of power by the High Court Division. We would like to observe that the High Court Division Rules permits a particular Judge to recall the unsigned order, but that must be done with notice to the parties. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">        </span></span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . (2 and 3)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.4pt; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For the Appellant:</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.4pt; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Mr. A.J Mohammad</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">Ali, Senior Advocate instructed</span> by Mr. Md. Taufique Hossain, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For Respondent Nos. 1(ka) &amp; 1 (gha):</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Mr. Omar Faruque, Advocate instructed by Mrs. Madhu Malati Chowdhury Barua, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Respondent Nos. 1 (Kha) &amp; 2-8:</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Not represented.</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-variant: small-caps; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah. J:</span></u></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> This petition for leave to appeal has been filed against the judgment and order dated the 9<sup>th</sup> day of March, 2011 passed by a learned Judge of the Single Bench of the High Court Division in Civil Revision No.3614 of 2004 discharging the Rule.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In this case we don’t feel the necessity to state the facts of the case inasmuch as Mr. A.J Mohammad Ali, learned Advocate appearing for the petitioner at the very outset, has drawn our attention to the orders of the concerned Bench which disposed the Rule. From the orders passed in the revision incorporated at page 95 of the paper book, it appears that the concerned bench made the civil revision out of list by its order dated 06.03.2006, then on 09.03.2011 recalled the unsigned order made on 06.03.2011 and then on that very date delivered the impugned judgment and order discharging the Rule in the absence of the petitionerr. We brought the records of the Civil revision from the High Court Division and on perusal of the order sheets, we found the facts as stated at page 95 correct. It struck our conscience how a learned Judge after recalling the order making a matter out of list hear the same on that the very date and dispose the same, in the absence of the petitioner.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">We deprecate this kind of exercise of power by the high Court Division. We would like to observe that the High Court Division Rules permits a particular Judge to recall the unsigned order, but that must be done with notice to the parties.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">In view of the above, we find no other alternative but to send the revision back to the High Court Division for hearing afresh and for disposal of the same in accordance with law on the evidence on record. Accordingly, this petition is disposed of in the following terms: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 26pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The impugned judgment and order of the High Court Division is set aside. The revision is sent back to the High Court Division for hearing afresh and for disposal in accordance with law on the evidence on record. Since, the revision is of the Year 2004, we feel that the same should be disposed of expeditiously. If so advised, the parties may mention the revision before the competent Bench for early hearing and if mentioned, the concerned Bench shall hear the same on priority absis.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-indent: 27pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Ed.</span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 90%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue__AUGUST_%2018(2)__C.%20P.%201260%20of%2011__Md.%20Abdul%20Wahhab%20Miah__AD__3.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 90%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Comic Sans MS'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL NO.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></u></strong></a><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 90%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Comic Sans MS'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">1260 OF 2011</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(From the judgment and order dated 9<sup>th</sup> March, 2011 passed by the High Court Division in Civil Revision No. 3614 of 2004).</span></p></div></div></div></div>
661	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Shahida Khatun Vs. Alhaj Abdul Malek Howlader &amp; ors., (Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL No. 3096 OF 2012  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J,  Muhammad Imman Ali, J,</p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Md. Harun-Ar-rashid, Advocate instructed by Syed Mahbubar Rahman, Advocate-on-Record.  ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ (AD)    </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2016</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Mst. Shahida Khatun </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Alhaj Abdul Malek Howlader being dead his heirs: 1(a) Parul Begum and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Civil Procedure </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-01</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">APPELLATE DIVISION</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">(CIVIL)</span></strong></span></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; height: 158px;" width="662"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes; height: 112.85pt;"><td style="width: 271.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J, </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Muhammad Imman Ali, J,</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 3.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">01.02.2016</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 46.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue__AUGUST_%2018(2)__C.%20P.%203096%20of%2012__Md.%20Abdul%20Wahhab%20Miah__AD__5.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11pt; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 300.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mst. Shahida Khatun</span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . Appellant </span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">-Versus</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">-</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Alhaj Abdul Malek Howlader being dead his heirs: 1(a) Parul Begum and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . Respondents</span></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: left;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 144</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">If the defendant succeeds to set aside the exparte decree he would to be without any remedy and he shall be surely entitled to restitution of possession of the suit land under section 144 of the Code.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">     </span>. . . (6)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Sections 144 and 151</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">It does not require any elaboration for the proposition that if fraud is detected Court can always act under section 151 of the Code, but when the decree passed in a suit or a case is in existence no relief can be given to the defendant by way of restitution or restoration of possession of the suit land wherein the plaintiff was put into the possession through due process of law.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                    </span>...(6)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; background: white;">For the Petitioner:</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; background: white;"> Mr. Md. Harun-Ar-rashid, Advocate instructed by Syed Mahbubar Rahman, Advocate-on-Record. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; background: white;">For Respondents:</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; background: white;"> Not represented.</span></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; font-variant: small-caps; background: white;">Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J:</span></u></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; background: white;"> This petition for leave to appeal has been filed against the judgment and order dated the 12<sup>th</sup> <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">day of June, 2012 passed by a learned Judge of the</span> <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">single Bench of the High Court Division in Civil</span> Revision No.700 of 2005 discharging the Rule.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Facts necessary to dispose this petition are that respondent No.1 as the plaintiff filed Title Suit No.284 of 2000 in the Court of Assistant Judge, Dohar for declaration of title and for recovery of khas possession. Subsequently, the suit being transferred to the Court of Assistant Judge, First Court, Dhaka was renumbered as Title Suit No.400 of 1997.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">In the suit the petitioner herein was defendant No.1. Eventually the suit was decreed exparte on 03.09.2002. The plaintiff levied Title Execution Case No.5 of 2002 for execution of the decree and pursuant to the decree, he was put into possession of the suit land. Thereafter, the defendant filed an application before the Execution Court under section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure (the Code) on 01.03.2004 with the prayer to put him into possession of the suit land on the ground that the plaintiff obtained the decree by practising fraud. The Execution Court by its order dated 03.10.2004 rejected the application.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Against the order of the Executing Court, the defendant filed Civil Revision No.302 of 2004 before the District Judge, Dhakia under section 115(2) of the Code. The learned District Judge. Dhaka summarily rejected the same on 03.10.2004. Against the order of the learned District Judge, the defendant filed Civil Revision No.700of 2005 before the High Court Division under section 115(4) of the Code and obtained a Rule. A learned Judge of the Single Bench by the impugned judgment and order discharge the Rule; hence this petition for leave to appeal.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">During hearing of the petition, it transpired that against the exparte decree the defendant had filed Title Appeal No.619 of 2002 before the District Judge, Dhaka and eventually the appeal was dismissed. Thus it is clear that the exparte decree is still in force.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 26.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Mr. Harun-Ar-Rashid, learned Advocate appearing for the petitioner has argued that since the exparte decree was obtained by practising fraud. The executing Court had power to put back the defendant into possession of the suit land. We cannot accept the submission of Mr. harun-Ar-Rashid for the simple reason that rightly or wrongly so long the decree remains that cannot be nullified or set at naught by putting the defendant into possession of the suit land which the plaintiff got through the due process of the in execution of the decree passed in the suit. We are of the view that if the defendant succeeds to set aside the exparte decree he would to be without any remedy and he shall be surely entitled to restitution of possession of the suit land under section 144 of the Code. Mr. Harun-Ar-Rashid has referred to some decisions in which the High Court Division and this Court as well interfered on the ground of fraud under section 151 of the Code. It does not require any elaboration for the proposition that if fraud is detected Court can always act under section 151 of the Code, but when the decree passed in a suit or a case is in existence no relief can be given to the defendant by way of restitution or restoration of possession of the suit land wherein the plaintiff was put into the possession through due process of law. We would like to observe further that since the appeal has been dismissed, the remedy of the defendant is to file revision application before the High Court Division. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">With above observation this petition is dismissed.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed.</span></strong></span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--></span><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><span style="color: #000000;"> <!--[endif]--> </span><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: left;"><span style="color: #000000;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue___August__18/Issue__AUGUST_%2018(2)__C.%20P.%203096%20of%2012__Md.%20Abdul%20Wahhab%20Miah__AD__5.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="color: #000000;" title=""><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">CIVIL</span></u></strong></a><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL No. 3096 OF 2012</span></u></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">(From the judgment and order dated 12<sup>th</sup> June, 2012 passed by the High Court Division in Civil Revision No. 700 of 2005).</span></span></p></div></div></div></div>
